In Experience 04, we are adding to the lab application <strong>five different ways to mark articles as read</strong>.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-image-group\" role=\"group\">\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_3435.png\" /></figure>\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_3436.png\" /></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Option 1.</strong> Tap on the check button on the top right of the page to mark the content of the page a read</p>\n<p><strong>Option 2.</strong> Long press on an article and mark the items before or after that article as read</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-image-group\" role=\"group\">\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_3437.png\" /></figure>\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_3438.png\" /></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Option 3.</strong> Use the swipe from right to left to mark a specific article as read (extend the gesture and hide the article)</p>\n<p><strong>Option 4.</strong> If you have auto-mark as read on scroll configured on Feedly Web, that setting will now be honored in the Lab app and articles will get automatically marked as read as you scroll. You can configure <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/account/mark-as-read\">auto-mark-as-read on-scroll in this preference section</a></p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-image-group\" role=\"group\">\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_3439.png\" /></figure>\n<figure><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/IMG_27E14B935EC3-1.jpeg\" /></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Option 5.</strong> At the end of each source and feed, there is a button to let you mark the articles you reviewed as read (and jump to the next source of feed)</p>\n<p>Finally, we fixed the swipe-to-close article bug (and added a symmetric gesture for people who prefer to swipe from the right)</p>\n<p><em>Three questions for the community:</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 1.</strong> Do the 2-level swipe left to &#8220;mark-as-read and hide&#8221; feel natural?</p>\n<p><strong>Question 2.</strong> Do these 5 mark as read options cover all your needs?</p>\n<p><strong>Question 3.</strong> What would be the top 1 or 2 features you would like to see added over the next 4 weeks for the Lab app to become your default reader?</p>\n<p>We created the Feedly Lab to give a voice to the community and make our development process more collaborative and transparent. So far the conversations have been very rewarding and insightful. Thank you!</p>\n<p>Looking forward to your input on this new experience on <strong>channel 04</strong> of the Feedly Lab Slack.</p>\n<p>-Edwin, Emily, and Petr</p>\n<p>Love the Web? allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n</div>\n<p>Reading shapes what you know, who you are, and how you think. Reading is your silent teacher and mentor. With <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/highlights\">the new highlights feature</a>, you can easily save the magic moments when you connect to new ideas – and come back to them more easily.</p>\n<div class=\"video-container display-mobile\">\n<p><iframe src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/175613659\" width=\"375\" height=\"667\" frameborder=\"0\" title=\"Highlighting on mobile\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n</div>\n<p>If you are not interested in using the new notes feature and would like to save the space at the top of your stories, there is <a href=\"http://feedly.com/i/preferences\">a preference knob in your preferences page</a> to turn this feature off.</p>\n<h2>Better WordPress Integration</h2>\n<div class=\"video-container display-desktop\">\n<p><iframe src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/175588520\" width=\"630\" height=\"375\" frameborder=\"0\" title=\"Share to wordpress\" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n</div>\n<p>If part of your workflow is saving excerpts of the best stories you discover in your feedly to one of your WordPress blogs, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro\">the new feedly Pro</a> will save you a lot of time.</p>\n<p>Simply click on the WordPress icon in the share toolbar and feedly will launch the WordPress PressIt window with the story you are reading. Quickly pick a picture, a category, or a tag, add your point of view and click on publish!</p>\n<p>You can also personalize the excerpt that gets associated with the story by selecting a snippet of text before clicking on the WordPress icon.</p>\n<p>WordPress is continuously improving their PressIt feature so we highly recommend upgrading to WordPress 4 if you want to benefit from the latest improvements.</p>\n<h2>IFTTT and Zapier</h2>\n<p>The new feedly Pro also includes a better integration with IFTTT and Zapier. <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro\">This new version</a> integrates with those platforms in real-time. For example, as soon as a story is saved to one of your personal knowledge boards (the new name for tags), all the recipes and zaps which are bound to that event are fired in real-time. We also improved the logic for image selection for recipes which require an image.</p>\n<h2>Faster Experience</h2>\n<p>We are working continuously behind the scenes to optimize feedly and add the hardware needed to keep feedly fast and boost your productivity. title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"http://feedly.com/i/library\" target=\"new\">Try Shared Collections Now</a><a class=\"callforaction secondary\" href=\"http://blog.feedly.com/2015/09/01/tips-to-make-most-of-shared-collections\" target=\"new\">Read Tutorial</a></p>\n<p>At feedly, we believe at our core that knowledge is power, and thus content is empowering—and even more so when you share it!</p>\n<p>So we are excited to introduce today a new <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/blog-shared-collections\" target=\"_blank\">feedly Pro</a> feature we call <strong>Shared Collections</strong>—a new and highly requested tool that lets you choose to share what you read with your teammates, colleagues, and followings.</p>\n<p>With Shared Collections, you can take the collections of reading sources you’ve already created—or create a new collection for the purpose of sharing—and make them public on one shared collections page dedicated just for you or your team. This Shared Collection page will showcase all of the blogs, publications, YouTube feeds, and Google News Alerts you want to showcase and make it easy for other people to follow the same sources with just a click. It&#8217;ll also allow you to create a personalized URL for your Shared Collections (nab the one you want today!).</p>\n<p>Take that Shared Collections page and use it to collaborate with others or to show the world what feeds your mind. You can even customize it to fit your company’s identity or your personal brand.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/screenshot-2015-09-01-08-15-18.png\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"visual alignnone wp-image-6880 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/screenshot-2015-09-01-08-15-18.png\" alt=\"Screenshot 2015-09-01 08.15.18\" width=\"414\" height=\"395\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/screenshot-2015-09-01-08-15-18.png 620w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/screenshot-2015-09-01-08-15-18-300x286.png 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 414px) 100vw, 414px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Shared Collections is completely opt-in. All of your collections default to private, so you can make use of this feature only if you want to. When you are ready to share, turn on the collections you want public and keep your personal collections private.</p>\n<h2>See Shared Collections in action.</h2>\n<p>See how ThoughtWorks, a consulting agency in San Francisco, has been using Shared Collections to collaborate across their organization and to scale their content marketing efforts:<br />\n<iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fTT1Clo5f3k\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<h2>Here are a few ways you can use your Shared Collections:</h2>\n<p><strong>Help your organization all follow the same publications, blogs, YouTube feeds, and Google Alerts.</strong> Empower your workforce to read and share.</p>\n<p><strong>Lead your industry by curating and sharing a rich list of must-follow reads.</strong> Lead others by showing them the important sources in your industry and move everyone forward together.</p>\n<p><strong>Help your teammates and peers find the best publications, blogs, YouTube feeds, and Google Alerts to do their jobs and join the conversation.</strong> Keep your teammates informed, moving in the same direction, and inspired with new ideas.</p>\n<p><strong>Make it easy to promote your company or agency’s thought leadership by putting all of your employees’ blogs and social media in one easy-to-follow branded page.</strong> Provide your customers, clients, social media following, and observers with a one-stop shop to find all of the resources created by your company. Perfect for any company in content marketing or with an employee social media program.</p>\n<p><strong>Organize your social media curation efforts by getting your team organized with the same sources.</strong> Need to feed the Content Monster? Arm your social media team with lots of publications and blogs to find entertaining posts.</p>\n<h2>Looking for some inspiration? Go to <a href=\"http://feedly.com/i/discover\" target=\"_blank\">http://feedly.com/i/discover</a> to browse other people’s Collections. Ask Leo to read and prioritize linked articles so you can avoid the overwhelm.</div>                  </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthis-is-the-title%2F&#38;linkname=Get%20tweets%20in%20Feedly\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthis-is-the-title%2F&#38;linkname=Get%20tweets%20in%20Feedly\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthis-is-the-title%2F&#38;linkname=Get%20tweets%20in%20Feedly\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthis-is-the-title%2F&#38;linkname=Get%20tweets%20in%20Feedly\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>Twitter is full of insightful news and trends. But integrating those insights into your research flow can be overwhelming and time-consuming. We hear from users all the time that you want to be able to bring parts of Twitter into your Feedly feeds for research and monitoring trends.<br><br>Today, we’re excited to share the new <span class=\"webfeeds-highlight\">Twitter Integration for Feedly!</span><br><br>You can follow Twitter accounts, hashtags, Lists, and searches. Even more exciting, <span class=\"webfeeds-highlight\">Feedly can pull content from linked articles directly into your feeds</span>. And Leo, your AI research assistant, can cut through the noise and prioritize or mute certain topics to make sure you only see tweets with essential information for your research.</p>\n\n\n\n<p></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-blockquote webfeeds-blockquote\">\n  <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__wrapper\">\n    <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__container\">\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__content\">One of my favorite features is the Feedly Twitter integration. I can stay informed about events and conversations I might otherwise miss, without it affecting how I use Twitter and cluttering up my feed.</p>\n      <img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Jon-Henshaw@3x.png\" class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__img\">\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__author\">Jon Henshaw, Founder of Coywolf</p>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-call-for-action-block webfeeds-call-for-action\"><div><h2 class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__title\">Get started with the Feedly Twitter integration</h2><p class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__sub\">Get your tweets in Feedly, and then let Leo filter out the noise. If you’re a Pro+, Business, or Enterprise user, connect your Twitter account now. If not, take a look at our plans so you can try it out.</p><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/twitter\" class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__button button accent primary small\">GET TWITTER INTEGRATION</a></p></div><figure><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Leo-Twitter.gif\" class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__img\"></figure><div></div></div>\n\n\n\n<p></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Follow Twitter accounts in Feedly</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Search for any Twitter handle in the Twitter feeds tab, just like you would with any other source on Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you search for an account, you’ll see two options: &#8216;<strong>Tweets</strong>&#8216; and &#8216;<strong>Tweets with Links</strong>&#8216;.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><span class=\"webfeeds-highlight\">Follow &#8216;<strong>Tweets</strong>&#8216; to see all tweets from an account.</span></p>\n\n\n\n<p><span class=\"webfeeds-highlight\">Follow &#8216;<strong>Tweets with Links</strong>&#8216; to follow only tweets from this account that link out to articles, videos, pictures, or any other type of external content. This lets you skip any tweets without external content. Choosing &#8216;Tweets with Links&#8217; is great because:</span></p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>If possible, we’ll extract the content of linked articles and make the content appear inline, just like any other article in your feeds.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>You can create a Leo priority on both the tweet and the content of the article when it’s extracted. We’ll tell you more about Leo priorities in a second.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p></p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large webfeeds-frame--no-shadow\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Follow-Twitter-Accounts@3x.png\"></figure><figcaption>Search for an account, and then choose whether you want to follow all tweets, or only tweets that link to external content.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Scan tweets — and the articles they link to — in your feeds</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Tweets are aggregated into your feeds with the rest of your content. When you click on a tweet that links to an article, the article will open in Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large wp-block-gts-feedly-image\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"600\" height=\"407\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Gif_1_with_background.gif\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14408\"/><figcaption>When a tweet links to an article, you can open the article right in Feedly.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Read and annotate linked articles directly in your Feedly</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ll pull the content of linked articles inline so you can read and annotate them in your Feedly. Add Notes or Highlights without having to click away to Twitter or another site to read or save the article.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"600\" height=\"407\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Gif_2_with_background.gif\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14410\"/><figcaption>Add Notes or Highlights to the linked article, save it to a board, or share it.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-blockquote webfeeds-blockquote\">\n  <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__wrapper\">\n    <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__container\">\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__content\">I can interact with tweets the same way I would with articles by saving, highlighting, and pushing them to other services. \n</p>\n      <img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Jon-Henshaw@3x.png\" class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__img\">\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__author\">Jon Henshaw, Founder of Coywolf</p>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<h2>Train Leo to prioritize specific topics, companies, or business events</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>This is where it gets powerful. Leo, your AI research assistant, helps cut through the noise of tweets in your feeds and find what’s essential to you.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large wp-block-gts-feedly-image\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"694\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-1024x694.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14400\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-1024x694.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-300x203.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-768x521.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-1536x1042.png 1536w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-2048x1389.png 2048w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-1200x814.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>Ask Leo to prioritize topics, like “TikTok”, and then use AND, OR, and NOT to refine your priority.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo will read both the content of the tweet and the article the tweet links to decide whether or not an article should be prioritized.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Train Leo to mute tweets that aren’t important to you</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Just like any other piece of content in Feedly, you can train Leo to mute tweets about topics you don&#8217;t care about, so you only see essential news in your feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large wp-block-gts-feedly-image\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"694\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-1024x694.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14399\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-1024x694.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-300x203.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-768x521.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-1536x1042.png 1536w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-2048x1389.png 2048w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-1200x814.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>You can ask Leo to mute any content related to a topic, like COVID-19.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Follow Twitter hashtags in Feedly</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can follow all tweets mentioning a specific hashtag. You’ll see two options, just like when following an account: &#8216;Tweets&#8217;, and &#8216;Tweets with Links&#8217;.<br><br>If you follow the hashtag #b2bmarketing, for example, you can choose:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>#b2bmarketing Tweets: all tweets will be pulled into your feeds</li><li>#b2bmarketing Tweets with Links: only tweets about #b2bmarketing that link to external content will be pulled into your feeds</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-frame--no-shadow\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Group-11.png\"></figure><figcaption>Follow all tweets with #b2bmarketing, or choose to follow only tweets that link to other content.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Follow Twitter Lists in Feedly</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also follow Twitter Lists, which are curated groups of Twitter accounts. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Follow both your own Lists and other users’ public Lists. Just paste the link of the Twitter List directly into the search bar in the Twitter feeds tab.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large wp-block-gts-feedly-image\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"666\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-1024x666.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14402\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-1024x666.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-300x195.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-768x500.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-1536x999.png 1536w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-2048x1332.png 2048w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-1200x781.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>Copy the URL of the List you want to follow, and paste it directly into Feedly.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Follow Twitter searches, or create advanced search queries to follow in Feedly</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Type your search directly into the search bar in Feedly, and the integration will continually pull updated results of the search into your feed.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here’s a helpful <a href=\"https://developer.twitter.com/en/docs/tweets/rules-and-filtering/overview/standard-operators\">list of Twitter’s standard operators</a> that you can use to refine your search.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large wp-block-gts-feedly-image\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"667\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-1024x667.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-14403\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-1024x667.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-300x195.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-768x500.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-1536x1000.png 1536w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-2048x1333.png 2048w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-1200x781.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>Type your search directly into Feedly to add it as a source. Use operators like -filter:retweets to remove retweets from the results.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also use the advanced search options on Twitter.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Once you’ve created an advanced search in Twitter, hit ‘Search’ and then paste the link to the advanced search directly into the search bar in your Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-blockquote webfeeds-blockquote\">\n  <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__wrapper\">\n    <div class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__container\">\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__content\">I was struggling to search through my bookmarked tweets on Twitter. But now I can follow my favorite Twitter users, star articles from Twitter and add them to boards. They are easily searchable and I can even annotate and highlight parts.</p>\n      <p class=\"webfeeds-blockquote__author\">David, professor at a large public university</p>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-call-for-action-block webfeeds-call-for-action\"><div><h2 class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__title\">Get started with the Feedly Twitter integration</h2><p class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__sub\">Get your tweets in Feedly, and then let Leo filter out the noise. If you’re a Pro+, Business, or Enterprise user, connect your Twitter account now. If not, take a look at our plans so you can try it out.</p><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/twitter\" class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__button button accent primary small\">GET TWITTER INTEGRATION</a></p></div><figure><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Leo-Twitter.gif\" class=\"webfeeds-call-for-action__img\"></figure><div></div></div>\n\n\n\n<p></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>FAQs about the Feedly Twitter integration</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">How do I get started with the Twitter integration? What can I follow?</h4>\n <div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n  <p>Anyone on a Pro+, Business, or Enterprise plan has access to the Twitter integration. Once you’ve connected your account to Twitter (go to the ‘Twitter feeds’ tab in Feedly to set it up) you can follow accounts, hashtags, searches, or Lists. </p>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Can I follow protected Twitter accounts? </h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n  <p>Yes. If the Twitter account you want to follow is protected, just make sure the Twitter account you&#8217;re using to connect to Feedly follows the protected account.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">How do I remove retweets?</h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p><p>\nRight now, it’s not possible to explicitly remove retweets. If you want to remove retweets from your feeds, our recommendation is to hide retweets from inside your Twitter account. <a href=\"https://help.twitter.com/en/using-twitter/retweet-faqs#:~:text=Select%20Turn%20off%20Retweets%20from,are%20already%20in%20your%20timeline.\">Here’s how</a></p> \n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Do I need to follow both “Tweets” and “Tweets with links” for an account or hashtag? </h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p>Nope. Choose “Tweets” and you’ll get all tweets, with and without links. If you follow “Tweets with Links,” you’ll only get tweets that link out to articles, videos, pictures, or any other type of external content.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Is it possible to filter a search further once I follow a hashtag?</h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n  <p>Yes. Our advice is to first use <a href=\"https://twitter.com/search-advanced?lang=en\">Twitter’s advanced search</a> to refine your search. Then, once you&#8217;re satisfied with the results, copy and paste the URL of the search in Feedly to create a new source.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Can I publish to Twitter from Feedly? </h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p>When you connect your Feedly to your Twitter account, this is a read-only connection allowing your Feedly to read tweets. Feedly will not write any tweets. To share insights from Feedly to Twitter, click the Twitter icon at the top of any article to generate a tweet and share your insights.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Can I follow my own Twitter account? </h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p>Of course! Follow the steps to follow a Twitter account. In the “Twitter Feeds” tab, search for your Twitter handle.</p>\n<p>You can choose to follow all tweets, or only tweets that link out to articles, so you’ll get the articles you share on Twitter right inside your Feedly.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">Will every single tweet from that hashtag get pulled into my feeds? </h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p>Yes. If you add a hashtag as a source, all the tweets generated for that hashtag will get pulled into your feed. If you’re getting too much noise from a hashtag, we recommend training Leo to prioritize or mute certain keywords or topics so that you only see what&#8217;s most important to you.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion\">\n <h4 class=\"webfeeds-accordion__title\">What’s the limit for articles from Twitter per day?</h4>\n<div class=\"webfeeds-accordion__content\">\n<p>Feedly has a limit of 5,000 articles per day from each Twitter source.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-related-post K","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Leo-Twitter.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx20/cdn13@2020_6/2020/08/16/13-38-59-072_c7db9e8be4c22d7b.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Jon-Henshaw@3x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn31@2020_1/2020/08/16/13-38-40-024_c20538361c4bfb36.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Follow-Twitter-Accounts@3x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn84@2020_4/2020/08/16/13-38-54-972_cc6855a8a82f09b7.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Gif_1_with_background.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn4@2020_2/2020/08/16/13-38-56-435_86657f088fc66d0f.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Gif_2_with_background.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn80@2020_5/2020/08/16/13-38-44-158_d49e615d2fbe1cc7.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Train-Leo@3x-1024x694.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn61@2020_2/2020/08/16/13-38-51-504_e4566a2f2cbfa494.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mute-Tweets@3x-1024x694.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn29@2020_3/2020/08/16/13-38-52-480_d5b119f6d9484b61.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Group-11.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn78@2020_5/2020/08/16/13-38-52-881_48ed813c8415c042.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-lists@3x-1024x666.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn44@2020_6/2020/08/16/13-38-46-298_fde30eb8af582b87.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Twitter-Searches@3x-1024x667.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn71@2020_3/2020/08/16/13-38-40-561_78417257d722ba8c.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"What Goes Down Better Come Up a.k.a. Adventures in Hbase Diagnostics","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=8329","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                      <img class=\"webfeeds-header__illustration webfeedsFeaturedVisual\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/servers.jpg\" width=\"960\" height=\"767\" />                                        <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                                      </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-goes-down-better-come-up-a-k-a-adventures-in-hbase-diagnostics%2F&#38;linkname=What%20Goes%20Down%20Better%20Come%20Up%20a.k.a.%20Adventures%20in%20Hbase%20Diagnostics\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-goes-down-better-come-up-a-k-a-adventures-in-hbase-diagnostics%2F&#38;linkname=What%20Goes%20Down%20Better%20Come%20Up%20a.k.a.%20Adventures%20in%20Hbase%20Diagnostics\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-goes-down-better-come-up-a-k-a-adventures-in-hbase-diagnostics%2F&#38;linkname=What%20Goes%20Down%20Better%20Come%20Up%20a.k.a.%20Adventures%20in%20Hbase%20Diagnostics\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-goes-down-better-come-up-a-k-a-adventures-in-hbase-diagnostics%2F&#38;linkname=What%20Goes%20Down%20Better%20Come%20Up%20a.k.a.%20Adventures%20in%20Hbase%20Diagnostics\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Earlier this year, the feedly cloud had a rough patch: API requests and feed updates started slowing down, eventually reaching the point where we experienced outages for a few days during our busiest time of the day (weekday mornings). For a cloud based company, being down for any period of time is soul-crushing never mind for a few mornings in a row. This led to a lot of frustration, late nights, and general questioning of the order of the universe. But with some persistence we managed to get through it and figure out the problem. We thought it may be some combination of instructive and interesting for others to hear, so we&#8217;re sharing the story. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But first we&#8217;d especially like to thank <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/larsgeorge\">Lars George</a>. Lars is a central figure in the <a href=\"http://hbase.apache.org\">HBase</a> community who has now founded a consulting company, <a href=\"http://www.opencore.com\">OpenCore</a>. It&#8217;s essentially impossible to find a great consultant in these situations, but through a bit of luck Lars happened to be in the Bay Area during this period and stopped by our offices for a few days to help out. His deep understanding of the HBase source code as well as past experiences was pivotal in diagnosing the problem.</span></p>\n<h2>The Cloud Distilled</h2>\n<p>Boiled down to basics, the feedly cloud does 2 things, downloads new articles from websites (which we call &#8220;polling&#8221;) and serve API requests so users can read articles via our website, mobile apps, and even third party applications like reeder. This sounds simple, and in some sense it is. Where it gets complex is the scale at which our system operates. On the polling side, there are about 40 million sources producing over 1000 articles every second. On the API side, we have about 10 million users generating over 200 million API requests per day. That&#8217;s a whole lotta bytes flowing through the system.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_8330\" style=\"width: 867px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-8330\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-8330 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05.png\" alt=\"feedly Cloud diagram\" width=\"857\" height=\"710\" data-wp-pid=\"8330\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05.png 857w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05-300x249.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05-768x636.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05-800x663.png 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 857px) 100vw, 857px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-8330\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">the main components of the cloud</p></div></p>\n<p>Due to this amount of data, the feedly cloud has grown significantly over the last 3 years: crawling more feeds, serving more users, and archiving more historical content – to allow users to search, go back in time, and dig deeper into topics.</p>\n<p>Another source of complexity is openness. As a co-founder, this is one aspect of feedly that I really love. We allow essentially any website to be able to connect with any user. We also allow 3rd party apps to use our API in their application. As an engineer, this can cause lots of headaches. Sourcing article data from other websites leads to all kinds of strange edge cases &#8212; 50MB articles, weird/incorrect character encodings, etc. And 3rd party apps can generate strange/inefficient access patterns.</p>\n<p>Both of these factors combine to make performance problems particularly hard to diagnose.</p>\n<h2>What Happened</h2>\n<p>We experienced degraded performance during the week of April 10th and more severe outages the following week. It was fairly easy to narrow the problem down to our database (HBase). In fact, In the weeks prior, we noticed occasional &#8216;blips&#8217; in performance and during those blips a slowdown in database operations, albeit on a much smaller scale.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_8336\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-8336\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-8336 size-medium\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-300x188.jpg\" alt=\"Artist depiction of the feedly cloud raining down destruction\" width=\"300\" height=\"188\" data-wp-pid=\"8336\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-300x188.jpg 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-768x480.jpg 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-1024x640.jpg 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-800x500.jpg 800w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning.jpg 1080w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-8336\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The feedly cloud was not so happy that week, my friends.</p></div></p>\n<p>Fortunately our ops team had already been collecting hbase metrics into a graphing system. I can&#8217;t emphasize how important this was. Without any historical information, we&#8217;d be at a total loss as to what had changed in the system. After poking around the many, many, many HBase metrics we found something that looked off (the &#8220;fsSyncLatencyAvgTime&#8221; metric). Better still, these anomalies roughly lined up with our down times. This led us to come up with a few theories:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>We were writing larger values. This could occur if user or article data changed somehow or due to a buggy code change.</li>\n<li>We were writing more data overall. Perhaps some new features we built were overwhelming HBase.</li>\n<li>Some hardware problem.</li>\n<li>We hit some kind of system limit in HBase and things were slowing down due to the amount or structure of our data.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Unfortunately all these theories are extremely hard to prove or disprove, and each team member has his own personal favorite. This is where Lars&#8217;s experience really helped. After reviewing the graphs, he dismissed the &#8220;system limit&#8221; theory. Our cluster is much smaller than some other companies out there and the configuration seemed sane. His feeling was it was a hardware/networking issue, but there was no clear indicator.</p>\n<h3>Theory 1: Writing Larger Values</h3>\n<p>This theory was kind of a long shot. The idea is that perhaps every so often we were writing really big values and that caused hbase to have issues. We added more metrics (this is a common theme when performance problems hit) to track when outlier read/write sizes occur, e.g. if we read or wrote a value larger than 5MB. After examining the charts, large read/writes kind of lined up with slowdowns but not really. To eliminate this as a possibility, we added an option to reject any large read/writes in our code. This wouldn&#8217;t be a final solution &#8212; all you oddballs that subscribe to 20,000 sources wouldn&#8217;t be able to access your feedly &#8212; but it let us confirm that this was not the root cause as we continued to have problems.</p>\n<h3>Theory 2: Writing More Data</h3>\n<p>This theory was perhaps more plausible than theory 1. The idea was that as feedly is growing, we eventually just reached a point where our request volume was too much for our database cluster to handle. We again added some metrics to track overall data read and write rates to hbase. Here again, things kind of lined up but not really. But we noticed we had high write volume on our analytics data table. This table contains a lot of valuable information for us, but we decided to disable all read/write activity to it as it&#8217;s not system critical.</p>\n<p>After deploying the change, things got much better! Hour long outages were reduced to a few small blips. But this didn&#8217;t sit well with us. Our cluster is pretty sizable, and should be able to handle our request load. Also, the rate of increase in downtime was way faster than our increase in storage used or request rate. So we left the analytics table disabled to keep performance manageable but continued the hunt.</p>\n<h3>Theory 3: Hardware Problem</h3>\n<p>As a software engineer this is always my favorite theory. It generally means I&#8217;ve done nothing wrong and don&#8217;t have to do anything to fix the problem. Unfortunately hardware fails in a myriad of oddball ways, so it can be very hard to convince everyone this is the cause and more importantly to identify the failing piece of equipment. This ended up being the root cause, but was particularly hard to pin down in this case.</p>\n<h2>How we Found the Problem and Fixed it</h2>\n<p>Here again, Lars&#8217;s experience helped us out. He recommended isolating the HBase code where the problem surfaced and then creating a reproducible test by running it in a standalone manner. So after about a day of work I was able to build a test we could run on our database machines, but independent of our production data. And it reproduced the problem! When debugging intermittent issues, having a reproducible test case is 90% of the battle. I was able to enable all the database log messages during the test and I noticed 2 machines were always involved in operations when slowdowns occurred, dn1 and dn3.</p>\n<p>I then extended the test to separately simulate the networking and disk write behavior the HBase code performed. This let us narrow down the problem down to a network issue. We removed the 2 nodes from our production cluster and things immediately got better. Our ops team found out the problem was actually in a network cable or patch panel. This was an especially insidious failure as it didn&#8217;t manifest itself in any machine logs. Incidentally, network issues was actually Lars&#8217;s original guess as to the problem!</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_8341\" style=\"width: 957px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-8341\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-8341 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency.png\" alt=\"sync latency\" width=\"947\" height=\"222\" data-wp-pid=\"8341\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency.png 947w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency-300x70.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency-768x180.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency-800x188.png 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 947px) 100vw, 947px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-8341\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The metric in question when we fixed the problem. Notice the immediate change in behavior.</p></div></p>\n<h2>Lessons Learned</h2>\n<p>The important thing when dealing with performance problems (outside of, you know, fixing them) is trying to learn what you did well and what you could have done better.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Things we did well:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Have a good metrics collection/graphing system in place.</strong> This should go without saying, but lots of times these types of projects can get delayed or deferred.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Get expert help.</strong> There&#8217;s lots of great resources out there. If you can&#8217;t find a great consultant, lots of people are generally willing to help on message boards or other places.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Stayed focused/methodical.</strong> It can get crazy when things are going wrong, but having a scientific process and logical way to attack the problem can make things manageable.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Dig into our tech stack.</strong> We rely almost exclusively on open source software. This enabled us to really understand and debug what was going on.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Things we could have done better:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Communicate.</strong> While Lars suggested networking, I initially discounted it since the problem manifested everywhere in our system, not just one machine. I would have learned there are some shared resources specific to data center build outs.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Gone more quickly to the hardware possibility.</strong> We did a lot of google searching for the symptoms we were seeing in our system, but there was not much out there. This is kind of an indicator something weird is probably happening in your environment. A hardware issue is pretty likely.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Attacked the problem earlier.</strong> As I mentioned, we had seen small blips prior to the outages and even done some (mostly unproductive) diagnostic work. Unfortunately not giving this top priority came back to bite us.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_8337\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-8337\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-8337 size-medium\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/cloud-300x200.jpg\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" data-wp-pid=\"8337\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/cloud-300x200.jpg 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/cloud.jpg 467w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-8337\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The feedly cloud today, hardy and hale.</p></div></p>\n<p>But there&#8217;s a happy ending to this story. As this post hopefully demonstrates, we&#8217;ve learned a lot and came out stronger: the feedly cloud is faster than ever and we have a much better understanding of the inner workings of HBase. We realize speed is very important to our users and will continue to invest in making the feedly Cloud faster and more resilient. Speaking of resilience, though we had a small downturn in <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/navbar\">feedly pro</a> signups in April, we are back to normal. This speaks to what a great community we have!</p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n           ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 13 Jul 2016 22:49:46 +0000","feedId":887,"bgimg":"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/servers.jpg","linkMd5":"89d490e5f7b9f6549c471fea26ca733f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn74@2020_4/2020/08/16/13-38-37-535_cc70180cf3982b62.webp","destWidth":960,"destHeight":767,"author":"kireet","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/servers.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn98@2020_4/2020/08/16/13-38-47-241_cc70180cf3982b62.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/Screenshot-2016-07-11-16.22.05.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn22@2020_2/2020/08/16/13-38-38-811_886f2e84e02c3213.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/lightning-300x188.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn88@2020_5/2020/08/16/13-38-40-563_b0053427b4f6017b.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/sync-latency.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx20/cdn97@2020_2/2020/08/16/13-38-53-104_4a38a323395f6365.webp","https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/cloud-300x200.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn18@2020_6/2020/08/16/13-38-54-954_48e03344b0a39b4c.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"Leo understands threat actor groups","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=13631","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                      <img class=\"webfeeds-header__illustration webfeedsFeaturedVisual\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/threat-actors-leo@2x.png\" width=\"552\" height=\"440\" />                                        <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                    <div class=\"webfeeds-header__subtitle\">Research threat actor groups and learn more about their tactics, techniques, and procedures, without the overwhelm.</div>                  </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-threat-actor-groups%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20threat%20actor%20groups\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-threat-actor-groups%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20threat%20actor%20groups\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-threat-actor-groups%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20threat%20actor%20groups\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-threat-actor-groups%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20threat%20actor%20groups\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>Cyber attacks continue to wreak havoc around the world. The actors waging these wars don’t just care about fraud either. They’re part of criminal organisations. Foreign governments stealing data for defense or national interests. Even terrorists or activists driven to disrupt and cause harm.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>What’s more, they’re increasingly capable and sophisticated. It’s a growing threat that can strike anyone at any time.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you learn about threat actors’ tactics and motivations, you can better prepare against them, saving you the costs and headaches that come with a breach or attack.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But there’s so much content to wade through when investigating these threat actors. It’s like fishing blind in an ocean. You’ll never know what’s coming back on the hook. More time and stress is spent on finding information about the threat, rather than acting on it. You can be overwhelmed.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’re passionate about helping you refine and streamline your open-source intelligence. That’s why we’ve taught Leo, <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">your AI research assistant</a>, to recognize threat actor groups. He can find them in your Feedly security feeds, prioritizing articles related to the actors and sectors you care about.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">try feedly for cybersecurity</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s imagine that you work in the telecommunications sector, and you’re researching the tactics and motivations of <a href=\"https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0069/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">MuddyWater</a>, an Iranian threat actor group.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Cut through the noise</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can train Leo to read all your cybersecurity, foreign affairs, and cyber warfare sources, and prioritize articles related to MuddyWater.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Threat-Actors-1.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Prioritize a threat actor</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo continuously reads the articles in your feeds and prioritizes the ones that mention MuddyWater (or any of its aliases). It’s a powerful and effective way to keep up with their latest techniques, tactics, and procedures.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>You’re in control</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo has been trained to recognize all the threat actor groups referenced by <a href=\"https://attack.mitre.org/groups/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">the MITRE ATT&#38;CK framework</a>. This is a list of common names for hacking groups, as recognized by the global security community.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Asking Leo to prioritize MuddyWater in your security feed is as simple as creating a new Topic priority and selecting ‘MuddyWater’ as the topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Threat-Actors-2.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Enter a threat actor alias in the topic field</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>When you prioritize MuddyWater, Leo will also look for other synonyms for that group like Seedworm and TEMP.Zagros.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo-and-topics/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">combine topics with +AND and +OR</a> to create even more targeted priorities for Leo. For example, use +AND to combine an actor group with an attack vector or a sector. This narrows his focus further so you find exactly what you’re looking for.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Continuously learning and getting smarter</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Because Leo is integrated with the MITRE ATT&#38;CK framework, it’s continuously learning and getting smarter. As new groups or aliases are identified, they’ll be automatically updated in your Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Threat-Actors-3.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo recognizes threat actor groups listed on the MITRE ATT&#38;CK framework</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Break down silos</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>As you search and discover new content, share insights with your research team. Together, you can create a Threat Intel Report Feedly Board and <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">bookmark the most critical insights you discover</a>. You can also add notes and highlights about why a threat is high-priority.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ve already seen security teams create tactical Boards, such as a Vulnerability Report, to share with their operations experts. You might also want to build a CISO Newsletter to keep your management updated. It’s all possible within Feedly.&#160;&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Articles bookmarked in a Board can be shared with the rest of the team via daily newsletters, Slack or Microsoft Teams notifications, or pushed to other apps using <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/the-feedly-cybersecurity-api/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">the Feedly Cybersecurity API</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/break-silos-1.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Share the threat intelligence you collect in Feedly with other teams and apps</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Streamline your open-source intelligence</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We’re excited to see how your security team will declutter your feeds and dig deeper into the critical threats that matter to you. Sign up today and discover <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/feedly-for-cybersecurity\">Feedly for Cybersecurity</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div Everyone can create new Personal Boards. Feedly Teams users will see separate lists in the left navigation for Personal and Team Boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>Feedly is turning its reader into a powerful knowledge board creation tool</p><cite>@sarahintampa / Techcrunch</cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<h2>How to Save an Article to a Board</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Boards are for saving and organizing articles. All Feedly plans (Basic, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/launch-board?utm_source=feedly&#38;utm_medium=blog&#38;utm_campaign=2017-launch-boards\">Pro</a>, and <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=feedly&#38;utm_medium=blog&#38;utm_campaign=2017-launch-boards\">Teams</a>) can&#160;save articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Click on the star on any article to save it. If this is your first time using Boards, we will ask you to create one.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-browser webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/socialmediaboard03-032717.png\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>When it comes to naming your Boards, try to keep a singular&#160;focus. This will keep you organized by your&#160;specific projects, clients, brands you monitor, or other important tasks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p class=\"webfeeds-pro-tips\">Save a single article to multiple Boards. In the&#160;example above, a piece about marketing tactics is saved to both the “Marketing &#38; Growth” and&#160;&#8220;Social Media&#8221; Boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Want to get started right now? Feedly Pro and Teams users can enrich articles using notes and highlights.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are part of a&#160;Feedly Teams plan, your teammates will be able to read your notes and add their own.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s a <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/add-note/\">step-by-step guide to adding notes</a> without missing a beat.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-browser webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/notes-032717.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Your note appears at the top of the article, where you can edit it or add another note right below it.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Highlight the most important passages to make it easy for your colleagues and other executives to scan. Since articles saved to Boards never expire, you’ll be able to revisit these notes and highlights in the future.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-browser webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/highlight-032717.png\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Shared Team Boards</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ve seen that active knowledge sharing can drive tons of value for your team. By creating shared Team Boards, you have a central place to store those gems you find and see what your teammates have saved.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Say goodbye to clunky email chains and spreadsheets. With Team Boards you have the additional option of sending email roundups to teammates as well as executives outside your team and even external clients. Here are some of their best practices that might inspire you: <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/examples-of-boards/\">7 Great Board Examples</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<section class=\"webfeeds-pro-tips\">Turn your <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/team-newsletters/\">Team Boards into newsletters</a>. It&#8217;s a great way to keep up with fast-changing industry trends as a team.</section>\n\n\n\n<h2>Save From Anywhere</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Easily switch between devices. The Feedly mobile apps (for <a href=\"https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/feedly-get-smarter/id396069556\">iPhone</a> or <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.devhd.feedly\">Android</a>) keep your content synced in real-time.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-iphone-x\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/mobile-story-033117.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Save to board on mobile</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can save content while browsing the web on desktop or mobile. Add the Feedly&#160;browser extension&#160;for <a href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/save-to-feedly-board/hdhblphcdjcicefneapkhmleapfaocih?hl=en-US\">Chrome</a>, <a href=\"https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/save-to-knowledge-board-feedly/\">Firefox</a>, and <a href=\"https://s3.feedly.com/release/feedly-tag.safariextz\">Safari</a>, and you can save any article in just two clicks. When you go back to your Boards on Feedly, the article will be right where you saved it.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/extension-040417.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>This Medium&#160;post is now saved to my &#8220;Entrepreneurship&#8221; Board in Feedly.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/notes\" class=\"button accent\">What Will YOU SAVE?</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<h2>FAQs</h2>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: How do I get my team started on Feedly?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team\">Start a one-month free trial</a> and invite as many teammates as you like. With Boards, you and your team can stay ahead of changes in your market, move faster than competitors, and plug knowledge gaps in your organization. We&#8217;re happy to work with your team through the one-month free trial and beyond.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Among the team here at Feedly, we use Boards every day to track mentions of our brand and share articles on topics such as machine learning, sales, and company culture.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: Can I&#160;save to Boards on my phone?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes. You can read, save, and share on mobile and desktop. If you’re reading on the <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/support/apps\">Feedly mobile app</a>, tap the <span class=\"display-icon\">icon to save. You’ll be able to save the current article to one or more of your Personal and Team Boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Don&#8217;t forget there are <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/5-ways-to-save-a-story/\">5 easy ways to save</a> to Boards!</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q:&#160;Can I add notes and highlights on my phone?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes, Feedly Pro and Teams users can use all the same features on mobile.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: Can I keep using Read Later?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes. Read Later is still&#160;there. You can save articles to Boards <em>and</em> Read Later for an even more customized Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: How are boards different from tags?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>We heard&#160;from users that it would be useful to be able to privately share content with teammates. Boards felt more like a central hub with&#160;shared access to&#160;allow for team curation. Tags didn&#8217;t meet the needs communicated to us by the Feedly community. Given that this is an area where we are going to invest a lot, we decided to change the terminology to have the right foundation in place.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you were using tags, all of your tags and the content associated with them are available as private personal Boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: How do I rename a board?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>When you are looking at one of your Boards, click on the [&#8230;] button and go to Settings. There you can change the Board name.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: How many boards can I create?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Feedly Pro and Teams accounts have unlimited Boards. Basic accounts can create up to 3 Boards. Feedly is proud to be supported by subscriptions to our premium feature set. <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/board-launch\">Compare&#160;the different features here</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: Is there a tutorial for adding notes and highlights?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes, here is a step-by-step <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/add-note/\">guide to adding notes</a>. And you can see <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/8-ways-to-use-feedly-boards-to-streamline-your-curation-process/#highlight\">how to create&#160;highlights</a> here.</p>\n                </div>\n   </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ffind-the-content-you-need-with-biopharma-search-mode%2F&#38;linkname=Find%20the%20content%20you%20need%20with%20Biopharma%20Search%20Mode\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>The amount of information published every day in the biopharma space is overwhelming and hard to skim through.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today we&#8217;re excited to announce the launch of <strong>Biopharma Search Mode</strong>, a tool that allows you to save time in your research flow. You can drill down into the specific content you want, beyond your existing feeds and sources. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>With Biopharma Search Mode, you can find articles you would have not found otherwise, discover new sources and save the pieces of content you find interesting. This feature is available to all Biopharma Enterprise users.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/chB0Eq?utm_source=xxxxx#id=xxxxx&#38;email=xxxxx&#38;wave=xxxxx&#38;plan=xxxxx&#38;enterprisename=xxxxx&#38;name=xxxxx&#38;feature=xxxxx\" class=\"button accent\">TRY FEEDLY FOR BIOPHARMA</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s walk through an example of how you could use Biopharma Search Mode to find articles you need. Imagine you lead an R&#38;D team at a biotech company and you want to learn about the latest breakthroughs related to cell therapies.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Create your search query</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>First, click on the search icon in the left navigation bar, and select &#8216;Search Across the Web&#8217;. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Type in a topic you want to research and select Biopharma Mode. When you search in Biopharma Mode, you&#8217;re searching across <strong>sources we&#8217;ve preselected based on biopharma users&#8217; favorite industry-specific sources</strong>, and you&#8217;ll get less noise.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screen-Shot-2020-08-11-at-5.34.41-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Go to the Power Search and select the Biopharma Mode</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>You&#8217;re in control</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Ask Leo to search for &#8220;cell therapy&#8221; in any of the biopharma sources we curated for you. Create a search query and select &#8220;cell therapy&#8221; as the topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can refine your query and&#160;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/power-search-across-the-web/\" target=\"_blank\">combine topics with +AND and +OR</a>. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can create even more targeted queries by selecting the types of publications you want on the left-hand side: pick from <strong>300 science journals,  800 biopharma trade publications, 80 regulatory sources, or 350 healthtech blogs</strong>. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, use +AND to focus on news related to cell therapies and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo-understands-biopharma-companies/\" target=\"_blank\">biopharma companies</a>, and select the Biopharma Business type of publications only.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screen-Shot-2020-08-11-at-5.41.37-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Refine the search query to cell therapy and biopharma companies among trade publications </figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Go further and refine your search by excluding certain topics, or by selecting &#8216;Title Only&#8217; vs &#8216;Entire Content&#8217;. Find more information about how to do this <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/power-search-across-the-web/\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Break down silos</h2>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Team Boards&#160;</strong>are the private spaces where you and your team can save the best content you discover in Feedly or on the web. You can bookmark, organize, and annotate content to share insights across your team and organization.<br><br>Once you’ve discovered a great new article, you can <strong>save it to a board</strong> and share it with the rest of your team via daily newsletters, Slack and Microsoft Teams notifications, or push it to other apps using our API.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screen-Shot-2020-08-11-at-5.49.09-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Save the most insightful content to your boards</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also click on the source name and see the other articles that the source has published. This is a powerful way to find new sources for niche topics. If the content is highly relevant, you can <strong>use the &#8216;Follow&#8217; button to add that new source</strong> to one of your Team Feeds and receive the next articles published by that source.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Streamline your biopharma intelligence</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We’re excited to see how your team will declutter your feeds and dig deeper into the biopharma news that matters to you.
