passed an exciting new milestone: 60,000 users have subscribed to feedly Pro. We would like to take a moment and thank each one of you and share some of the projects we are working on, thanks to this new funding.</span><span id=\"more-7093\"></span></p>\n<p><b>1. More servers </b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">&#8211; The feedly cloud is connected to 42,000,000 feeds of information, receiving about 50,000,000 new stories every day. We are adding servers to the feedly Cloud to store, organize, and index all of this information so that we can continue to serve you feedly very fast.</span></p>\n<p><b><b><span style=\"color:#2bb24c;\"> </span></b>2. Feedly login</b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\"><span style=\"color:#2bb24c;\"><strong> (#delivered / Nov 16th 2015 / <a href=\"http://blog.feedly.com/2015/11/11/a-new-feedly-login/\">Announcement</a>)</strong></span> &#8211; This is something </span><a href=\"http://feedly.uservoice.com/forums/192636-suggestions/suggestions/3754612-create-a-feedly-login-option-to-access-without-goo\"><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">a lot of users have been requesting</span></a><span style=\"font-weight:400;\"> for some time. We now have the resources to fund this project and make it a reality. We will continue to offer the ability to log in with Google, Facebook, Twitter, Microsoft, and Evernote to people who prefer to use existing logins. We are also adding support for logging in with Slack and Office 365, since we hear that it will make logging in even easier for some of our users.</span></p>\n<p><b>3. Shared tags </b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">&#8211; When we released Shared Collections last month, some users asked us to go one step further and also allow them to share some of their tags. We really like this idea and are working on both continuing to enhance Shared Collections and adding shared tags.</span></p>\n<p><b>4. Filtering, saved search, and noise reduction</b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\"> &#8211; We have been hearing a lot of murmurs from you around the need for filtering and for alerts. We are going to use part of the new Pro funding for a project that will allow you to define manual and automated filters. It will also allow you to save searches as alerts. We love the idea of giving you even more control over how to tailor your feedly. More signal, less noise.</span></p>\n<p><b>5. Better Slack integration</b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\"> &#8211; We think that we can reduce some of the friction that exists around manually sharing stories from your feedly into your Slack channels. Many users are  using feedly and Slack in tandem, so we are going to invest some time enhancing the integration.</span></p>\n<p><b>6. Fewer iOS crashes <span style=\"color:#2bb24c;\"><strong>(#delivered / Oct 21st 2015 / <a style=\"color:#2bb24c;\" href=\"http://blog.feedly.com/2015/10/21/safari-view-san-francisco-and-3d-touch-new-feedly-for-ios/\">Announcement</a>)</strong></span></b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">&#8211; We have been receiving some reports of iOS crashes. They seem related to loading web pages, videos, and animated gifs within feedly. We hate crashes as much as anyone else, and we are fixing this. We are investing time into a new update of the feedly iOS application which changes how we load content and minimizes the risk of the application crashing. We are also investing time optimizing how we serve content to minimize battery usage. You should see the fruits of this work in the v30 update of the app which should be available within a few weeks.</span></p>\n<p><b>7. Team edition</b><span style=\"font-weight:400;\"> &#8211; More on that soon&#8230;</span></p>\n<p>Thanks to your backing, we’re able to continuously invest in building a better, faster, stronger and more useful work newsfeed. It is a great pleasure to serve you.</p>\n<p>Edwin, Noelle and Remi</p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n           ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 16 Oct 2015 06:27:50 +0000","feedId":887,"bgimg":"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/screenshot-2015-10-15-15-53-38.png","linkMd5":"f6a0741ddcb9d7f50ec364a243a34bc3","author":"@feedly","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/screenshot-2015-10-15-15-53-38.png":null}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"New AI-Driven Discovery Experience","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=10840","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                                                            <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                                      </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-discovery%2F&#38;linkname=New%20AI-Driven%20Discovery%20Experience\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-discovery%2F&#38;linkname=New%20AI-Driven%20Discovery%20Experience\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-discovery%2F&#38;linkname=New%20AI-Driven%20Discovery%20Experience\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-discovery%2F&#38;linkname=New%20AI-Driven%20Discovery%20Experience\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p></p>\n\n\n<p>We love the Web because it is an open and distributed network that offers everyone the freedom and control to publish and follow what matters to them.</p>\n<p>We also love the web because it has enabled a new generation of content creators (<a href=\"https://stratechery.com/\">Ben Thompson</a>, <a href=\"https://www.schneier.com/\">Bruce Schneier</a>, <a href=\"https://www.swiss-miss.com/\">Tina Eisenberg</a>, <a href=\"https://www.sethgodin.com/\">Seth Godin</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/\">Maria Popova</a>, etc.). Those independent thinkers continuously explore the edge of the known and share insightful and inspiring ideas with their communities.</p>\n<p>Connecting people to the best sources for the topics that matter to them has been core to our mission since the very start of Feedly.</p>\n<p>But discovery is a hard problem. The web is organic, a reflection of the global community&#8217;s changing needs and priorities. There are millions of sources across thousands of topics and we all have a different appetite when it comes to feeding our minds.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-04-22.13.47.png\"><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>About twelve months ago, we created a machine learning team to see if the latest progress in deep learning and natural language processing could help us crack this nut.</p>\n<p>Today, we are excited to give you a preview of the result of that work with the release of the new discovery experience in the Feedly Lab app (Experience 06).</p>\n<h2>Two thousand topics</h2>\n<p>The first discovery challenge is to create a taxonomy of topics.</p>\n<p>You can think of Feedly as a rich graph of people, topics, and sources. To build the right taxonomy, we started with the raw data on all of Feedly’s sources. We had to create a model to clean, enrich, and organize that data into a hierarchy of topics. <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/data-science-behind-recommendations-in-feedly/\">Learn more about the data science behind this</a>.</p>\n<p>The result is a rich, interconnected network of two thousand English topics. And it’s mapped well with how people expect to explore and read on the Web.</p>\n<p>Some topics are broad: <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/tech-blogs\">tech</a>, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/security-blogs\">security</a>, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/design-blogs\">design</a>, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/marketing-blogs\">marketing</a>. Some are very niche: <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/ar-blogs\">augmented reality</a>, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/malware-blogs\">malware</a>, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/typography-blogs\">typography</a>, or <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/top/seo-blogs\">SEO</a>.</p>\n<p>On the discovery homepage, we showcase thirty topics based on popular industries, trends, skills, or passions. You can access all of the topics in Feedly via the search box.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-04-21.17.19.png\"><p></p>\n<p></p>\n<figcaption></figcaption>\n</figure>\n<h2>The fifty most interesting sources</h2>\n<p>The second discovery challenge is to find the fifty most interesting sources someone researching any topic might want to follow.</p>\n<p>Ranking sources is hard because not all sources are equal. In tech as an example, you have mainstream publications like The Verge or TechCrunch, expert voices like Ben Thompson, and lots of B-list noisy sources which don&#8217;t add much value.</p>\n<p>In addition, for niche topics like virtual reality, some sources are specific to VR while others cover a range of related topics.</p>\n<p>To solve this challenge, we created a model which looks at sources through three different lenses:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>follower count</li>\n<li>relevance (how focused is the source on the given topic)</li>\n<li>engagement (a proxy for quality and attention)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The outcome is new search result cards. You can explore the fifty most interesting sources for a given topic and sort them using the lens that is most important to you.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-04-21.21.10.png\"><p></p>\n<p></p>\n<figcaption></figcaption>\n</figure>\n<h2>Neighborhoods</h2>\n<p>One of the benefits of the new topic model is that the 2,000 topics are organized in a hierarchy. This makes it easy for you to zoom in or out and explore many different neighborhoods of the Web.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screen-Shot-2018-08-27-at-1.50.03-PM.png\"><p></p>\n<p></p>\n<figcaption></figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>For example, from the cybersecurity topic, you can jump to a list of related topics that let you dig deeper into malware, forensics, or privacy.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-04-21.22.57.png\"><p></p>\n<p></p>\n<figcaption></figcaption>\n</figure>\n<h2>One more thing…</h2>\n<p>We have done a lot of research over the last four years to understand how people discover new sources. One insight we learned is that people often co-read certain sources. For example, if you are interested in art, design, and pop culture and you follow Fubiz, there is a high chance that you also follow Designboom.</p>\n<p>With that in mind, we spent some time creating a model that learns what sources are often co-read. The idea is that a user could enter a source that they love and discover another source they could pair it with.</p>\n<p>You can learn more about the machine learning model (we call it feed2vec) powering this experience through <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/data-science-behind-recommendations-in-feedly/\">the article Paul published here</a>.</p>\n<p>As a user, you can access this feature by searching in the discover page for a source you love to read. The result will be a list of sources which are often co-read with that source.\n</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-04-21.25.47.png\"><p></p>\n<p></p>\n<figcaption></figcaption>\n</figure>\n<h2>Thank you!</h2>\n<p>I would like to thank Paul, Michelle, Mathieu, and Aymeric for the great research work they did to take this project from zero to one. People who have tried to tackle discovery know that it is a very hard challenge and the results of this project have been very impressive.</p>\n<p>We would also like to thank the community for participating in the Battle of the Sources experiment. Your input was key in helping us learn how to model the source ranking. We are going to continue to invest in discovery and we look forward to continuing to collaborate with you.</p>\n<p>We would also like to thank Dan Newman, Daron Brewood, Enrico, Joey, Lior, Paul Adams, Ryan Murphy, and Joseph Thornley from the Lab for reviewing an earlier version of this article.</p>                </div>\n            \n\n Novartis, and 23&#38;Me.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img articles in our feed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>As you can see, a considerable amount of these articles are market reports. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s train Leo to read this feed and filter out all the noisy market reports.<br></p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can create a new Leo mute filter by click on the Train Leo button and selecting the Mute Filters skill.<br></p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img filter</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>In the Mute Filters editor, search and select the Market Reports smart topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img topic</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can see a preview of all the articles that Leo has read and recognized as Market Reports.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Screen-Shot-2020-03-13-at-1.22.39-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo mutes articles he recognizes as market reports</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo will continuously read your feed and remove market reports, letting you focus on the topics and trends that matter to you.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure market reports</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p></p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>The Leo Market Report mute filter helps us cut through the noise and track company updates a lot more ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 10 Jul 2018 14:01:26 +0000","feedId":887,"bgimg":"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/seo-onboarding@2x.png","linkMd5":"3641df72ee5a1cd18b6b337f25a9347f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn5@2020_1/2020/08/16/13-38-36-519_76b5523d4e792b6a.webp","destWidth":1022,"destHeight":660,"author":"Edwin K","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/07/seo-onboarding@2x.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn99@2020_3/2020/08/16/13-38-41-921_76b5523d4e792b6a.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"The Feedly Cybersecurity API","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=13594","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                      <img class=\"webfeeds-header__illustration webfeedsFeaturedVisual\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/cloud-APIs-leo@2x.png\" width=\"552\" height=\"440\" />                                        <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                    <div class=\"webfeeds-header__subtitle\">Feedly for Cybersecurity includes an API that allows cybersecurity teams to share the threat intelligence they collect in Feedly with other applications.</div>                  </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthe-feedly-cybersecurity-api%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Feedly%20Cybersecurity%20API\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthe-feedly-cybersecurity-api%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Feedly%20Cybersecurity%20API\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthe-feedly-cybersecurity-api%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Feedly%20Cybersecurity%20API\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fthe-feedly-cybersecurity-api%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Feedly%20Cybersecurity%20API\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>150,000 cybersecurity professionals use Feedly to collect intelligence about the evolving threat landscape.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Threat research and collection are one step of the overall threat intelligence, investigation, and response.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Feedly Cybersecurity API allows security teams to easily integrate the insights they collect in Feedly into other systems and applications. Some teams use the API to extract data about threats and vulnerabilities and feed larger machine learning threat-prioritization models. Some teams use the API to create Jira tickets based on the content of the Feedly boards to make sure that critical vulnerabilities are reviews and patched in a timely manner.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Access to the Feedly API (up to 200,000 requests per month) is an add-on included in the Enterprise Edition of the Feedly for Cybersecurity package.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">TRY FEEDLY FOR CYBERSECURITY</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>In this tutorial, we will show you how to use the Feedly API to access the content of your security feeds, your boards, and your Leo priorities.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Authentication</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>When you subscribe to Feedly for Cybersecurity Enterprise Edition, we will provide you with a special Feedly access token associated with your account. That token will allow you to access the content of your feeds, boards, and priorities and perform up to 200,000 requests per month.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Articles as JSON</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The JSON representation of an article combines some of the open-source content included on the RSS or on the website, CVE/CVSS/Exploit information aggregated from vulnerability and exploit databases, as well as the results of the Leo cybersecurity models.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The title, content, and visual information give you access to the core of the content of the articles:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/json-article-core.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>JSON representation of the core of the article</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>The commonTopics array represents Leo’s topic classification. The entities represent CVEs, products, or companies Leo has identified in the article. The CVE entity includes CVSS and exploits information extracted from vulnerability databases.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The estimatedCVSS represents the result of Leo’s CVSS scoring model. This is useful for zero-days and articles which do not mention a CVE explicitly. In those cases, Leo reads the content of the article and computes an approximative CVSS score based on the terminology used in the article or the tweet.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/json-leo-enrichment.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo enrichment of the article</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Pro tip: When you have an article open in the Feedly web application, you can use the Shift+D keyboard shortcut to see and inspect the JSON of the article.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/shift-d-show-article-json.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Use keyboard shortcut SHIFT+D to see the preview of the article JSON</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Accessing the content of your feeds</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s imagine that you have a “Security News” feed which contains a list of known and trusted security sources you want to follow.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Feedly API allows you to query Feedly and ask for the last 100 articles aggregated in that feed. The articles are normalized in a JSON format which includes the title, the content, the source information, as well as all some cybersecurity metadata (Leo topics classification, CVE metadata, CVSS metadata, exploit information.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can use the <a href=\"https://developer.feedly.com/v3/streams/\">Stream endpoint</a> to get the last 100 articles published in a feed:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/stream-api.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Overview of the stream endpoint</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The most important parameter is the streamId</strong>. Each feed in your Feedly account has a unique stream id. When you select the feed in the left navigation bar, you see the streamId as part of the URL. The stream id is formatted as `enterprise/xxxx/category/xxxx` for team feeds and `user/xxxx/category/xxxx` for personal feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/finding-feed-streamId.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Finding the streamId of a feed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>The <strong>count parameter</strong> defines the number of articles the server will return. We recommend that you select a number between 20 and 100. If you need access to more than 100 articles, you can use the <strong>continuation parameter</strong> returned by the response to chain the requests and ask for the next 100 articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Finally, the <strong>importantOnly parameter</strong> allows you to&#160;get the list of articles in the stream that has been prioritized by Leo.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Troubleshooting tips:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Make sure that the requests you are making are authenticated using the token you have received from the Feedly team.</li><li>Make sure that the streamId is URL encoded when it is passed as a parameter to the Stream endpoint.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>Accessing the content of your boards</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Security teams use boards to bookmark critical articles everyone in the team should be aware of. They also often use boards to bookmark articles they want to share with other applications.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can use the same Stream endpoint to access the last N articles manually bookmarked by your team to a board.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The only difference will be the streamId. Team Board streamIds are formatted as `enterprise/xxxx/tag/xxxx`. Personal Board streamIds are formatted as `user/xxxx/tag/xxxx`.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/finding-board-streamId.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Finding the streamId of a board</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If users have annotated the articles with some notes and highlights while saving the article to a board, those notes and highlights will be included in the article JSON structure.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/json-notes-and-highlights.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>JSON of notes and highlights</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Example: Integrating Feedly with your ticketing system</h2>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/API-example.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Here is an example of how you can streamline the integration between the research and collection work of your threat intelligence team and the analysis and patching work of your operations team.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The research team creates a Feedly board called Critical Vulns where why bookmark articles related to critical vulnerabilities they want the operations team to be aware off and review.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Each time the research team finds a critical insight, they save that article in the Critical Vulns board, adding a note about why they think the vulnerability needs to be reviewed and patched.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead of asking the research team to manually create a ticket in your ticketing system (Jira, Service Now, etc.), you can write a small app which every 5 minutes connect to the Critical Vulns board, requests the last 20 articles bookmarked in that board, and for each new article, used the API of your ticketing system to create a new ticket. The app can enrich the ticket with the URL of the article saved in the board, the CVE information, and the notes and highlights from the researcher.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is a powerful way to break the silos between your research team and your operations team and make sure that critical vulnerabilities are patched faster.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Pro tip: there is a simple solution to finding the new articles saved in a board. When your app processes a list of articles, it should save the first article in the list and the next time it uses the Stream Feedly app to get the latest articles bookmarked to a board, your app can use the <strong>newerThan parameter</strong> of the /v3/stream/content and pass that article id instead of a timestamp to get newer articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>A lot more…</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The Feedly web application and mobile applications are built on top of the Feedly API. This means that every piece of information available in the application and every action taken in the application is available in the API.<br><br>For more information about the Feedly API, please visit the <a href=\"https://developer.feedly.com/\">Feedly Developer Website</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Streamline your open-source intelligence</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We are excited to see many security teams use the Feedly API to streamline their open-source threat intelligence process. Sign up today and discover what Feedly for Cybersecurity can do for you!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">TRY FEEDLY FOR CYBERSECURITY</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are interested in learning more about Leo’s roadmap, you can join the <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/slack-community/\">Feedly Community Slack</a>. 2020 will be a thrilling year with new skills and bold experiments!</p>\n title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>If you’re like us, you might have been hearing the term “social selling” at an <a href=\"http://blog.feedly.com/2016/03/10/trend-acceleration-ideas-are-moving-faster-and-faster-can-we-keep-up/\" target=\"_blank\">increasingly frequent rate</a>. We hear it at conferences, in LinkedIn forums, in team meetings, on Twitter, and on billboards.</p>\n<p>With social experiences like Twitter and Facebook becoming core to the web, this concept of social selling has become a definitive new approach for the ways that organizations think about building relationships. It is a methodology that embraces at its center a driving belief for us at feedly: Content is a currency. That is, that high quality content is more than just an entertaining read. Content builds relationships, drives business, and steers innovation.</p>\n<p>In fact, as we’ve talked with more and more of you as part of our regular product development process, we’ve learned that many of you are using feedly as a core content engine to drive your social selling. Many of you are using feedly as your main hub to organize your favorite sources, feed yourself with daily reading, and then deciminate the best stories to your customers.</p>\n<h2>But just what is social selling?</h2>\n<p>Social selling is the idea of using content—mostly online—to help educate prospective customers, build a relationship with them, and help guide them to a purchase decision.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7841\"></span></p>\n<p>Sometimes this means that sales people build personas and share relevant information through social channels like LinkedIn, Twitter, YouTube, and more. Sometimes it means emailing interesting, relevant content to prospective customers. All of these activities overlap with a bunch of other trends that people have been buzzing about: sales enablement, employee advocacy, personal branding, social media marketing, content marketing, inbound marketing, and more.https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pkap9qDYnlY</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"https://goo.gl/TQj0XN\" target=\"new\">Learn more about Social Selling and feedly</a></p>\n<p>A salesperson at a content marketing company, for instance, might share content on her LinkedIn about why good content is important. Or a digital marketing firm might post about the decline of old ad formats and the latest information about the new ones.</p>\n<p>Yes, put another way, social selling is a way to drive revenue using content.</p>\n<h2>Is it really becoming more popular?</h2>\n<p>According to some sources, yes, it is:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"http://blog.hubspot.com/sales/surprising-statistics-on-social-selling\" target=\"_blank\">71 percent</a> of sales people believe that their role is changing and will be radically different in five years.</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://blog.hubspot.com/sales/surprising-statistics-on-social-selling\" target=\"_blank\">69 percent</a> of sales executives believe that the buying process is changing faster than organizations are responding to it.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://blogs.oracle.com/marketingcloud/3-compelling-stats-that-make-the-case-for-social-selling-for-b2b\" target=\"_blank\">75 percent</a> of B2B buyers use social media to be more informed about vendors.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Why? Because statistics are showing that the methodology could be pretty effective.</h2>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"http://blog.hubspot.com/sales/social-selling-stats-that-will-inspire-you\" target=\"_blank\">98 percent</a> of sales reps with more than 5,000 LinkedIn connections meet or surpass quota.</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://postbeyond.com/why-social-selling-infographic/\" target=\"_blank\">40 percent</a> of salespeople have closed two to five more deals per year as a result of social selling.</li>\n<li>Bain &#38; Company found that a <a href=\"http://postbeyond.com/why-social-selling-infographic/\" target=\"_blank\">12 percent</a> increase in brand advocacy generates 2X increase in revenue growth</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://postbeyond.com/why-social-selling-infographic/\" target=\"_blank\">73 percent</a> of salespeople using social selling as part of their sales process outperformed their sales peers and exceeded their quotas 23 percent more often.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Where can you learn more?</h2>\n<p>Over the coming weeks, we’ll be exploring more about using social selling to help your business. strong!</p>\n<p>This move to a more open and transparent process has been extremely rewarding: we are collecting great ideas and getting instant feedback on some of the bolder changes we are exploring. (<em>See the detailed changelog below.</em>)</p>\n<p>We are also getting a lot of great bug reports. Thank you!</p>\n<p>Our focus over the past 10 days was to address those bugs and polish the new experience (including <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-01-smooth-scrolling/\">scrolling</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-03-access-all-your-feeds-boards-and-sources/\">navigation</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-02-title-only-magazine-and-card-views/\">views</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-04-mark-as-read/\">mark-as-read options</a>, and <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-05-night-mode/\">night mode</a>) so that we have a solid foundation to invite more people to the Lab and explore new ideas.</p>\n<p><em>Three questions for the community:</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 1:</strong> We did some night mode color tuning. Better? If not, can you please let us know 1/ if there is a specific part of the theme we need to refine, and 2/ what is your luminosity level?</p>\n<p><strong>Question 2:</strong> Are there other bugs you would like us to fix? Please post them in the &#8220;bugs&#8221; channel in Slack.</p>\n<p><strong>Question 3:</strong> Is there a missing feature which is not currently in <a href=\"https://trello.com/b/bPZDVlwx/feedly-mobileai-lab\">the Trello roadmap</a> that is preventing you from adopting the new app? Please post it in the &#8220;general&#8221; channel.</p>\n<p>We love building the new Feedly in the open and look forward to the next 12 weeks!</p>\n<p><em>Here is a more detailed changelog for this week&#8217;s bug hunt:</em></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Scroll and tap to open conflict (via Jesse Flanagan, John, and Kireet)</li>\n<li>Empty screen when loading an article after switching app (via Ryan)</li>\n<li>Improve scrolling performance (via Chad Hudson and Cyril)</li>\n<li>Double tap on selected bottom tab bar should scroll to the top (via Lior)</li>\n<li>Contextual mark as read copy improvement (mark all as read versus mark current top articles as read)</li>\n<li>Mark as read missing items (via Dan Newman)</li>\n<li>Mark as read and refresh of the All section (via Eric L.)</li>\n<li>Move to next feed and gray out articles after Mark all as read (via Serge Courrier)</li>\n<li>Night mode: Improve the brightness/contrast of the mark-as-read notification (via Dan Newman)</li>\n<li>Night mode: Better read vs unread distinction (via Lee Sprung)</li>\n<li>Night mode: Article separators (via Daniel)</li>\n<li>Read later tab is not selected (via Lior)</li>\n<li>Toggle read later bug (via Lior)</li>\n<li>Do not automatically mark-as-read articles that the user manually kept unread (via Gabe)</li>\n<li>Auto-mark-as-read-on-scroll: improvements regarding marking-as-read the last articles on the page</li>\n<li>Refresh automatically when the user launches the app after minutes (via sryo)</li>\n<li>Speed up the close animation (Aaron M.)</li>\n<li>Make compact view even more compact by inlining the source and date metadata</li>\n<li>Mark-all-as-read button at the end of a list of articles</li>\n<li>Second level left-to-right gesture to trigger the save to board action (via Eiselch)</li>\n<li>Progress circle needs to be reset after changing sort or layout preference (via John)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Thank you for your time and width=\"282\" height=\"557\" /></center>The first experiment of <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/introducing-the-mobileai-lab/\">the Mobile+AI Lab</a> is around the scrolling experience in the mobile app.</p>\n<p>The main purpose of the Feedly mobile app is to allow you to quickly skim through 50 to 100 articles, pick and read 3 to 10 of them, and share or save the most interesting ones.</p>\n<p>How easily and naturally you skim through articles is the most important part of the experience.</p>\n<p>In the existing Feedly mobile app, we have a paged scrolling experience — mainly for performance reasons.</p>\n<p>Given that we are starting the new Feedly mobile application from scratch, we thought that it would be interesting to explore a smooth scrolling experience and see if it makes skimming through 50 to 100 articles more seamless and effortless.</p>\n<p><em>Questions for the Lab participants:</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 1. </strong>Download the Feedly Lab iOS app and log into your Feedly account. Scroll through your Today stream, and then let us know if the new scrolling experience feels better than the current paged scrolling.</p>\n<p><strong>Question 2. </strong>On average, how many articles can you scroll through before your eyes get tired?</p>\n<p>Looking forward to talking more about this in the Lab Slack channel! href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fhow-feedly-changed-my-career-as-an-art-curator%2F&#38;linkname=How%20feedly%20Changed%20My%20Career%20as%20an%20Art%20Curator\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fhow-feedly-changed-my-career-as-an-art-curator%2F&#38;linkname=How%20feedly%20Changed%20My%20Career%20as%20an%20Art%20Curator\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p><em>You, our users, use feedly for such a wide range of jobs. Today we&#8217;d like to showcase a member of the feedly community who uses it as a curator of digital art, a burgeoning sector. Ryan Cowdrey, of the young startup <a href=\"http://23Vivi.com\" target=\"_blank\">23VIVI.com</a>, shows us how you can use feedly to leverage content as an art curator. He provides a guest post for us today.</em></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">My name is Ryan Cowdrey and I’m the Director of Curation at <a href=\"http://23Vivi.com\" target=\"_blank\">23VIVI.com</a>, an online marketplace that offers rare and limited edition digital art. For your enjoyment, I pose the question:</span></p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“With so much digital media content at one’s fingertips at all times, how does a creative individual discover the latest trends amongst all the noise out there?”</span></p></blockquote>\n<p>Being an art curator in the digital age requires strategic tools for effectively treading through the massive amount of content that we can access. Curators are relying more and more on internet sources to get content updates that they need on a daily basis. (Blouin ArtInfo, ArtNet News, Design Collector, Fubiz, BOMB Magazine, Colossal, to name a few.)</p>\n<p>Not to mention that if you curate digital art exclusively, you are now relying solely on internet sources to get your art fix. The tools that one uses to augment their curation efforts will set them apart from the rest.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7808\"></span></p>\n<p>As a digital art curator at 23VIVI.com, I follow upwards of 30 big-time art magazines to stay up to date on art creation and news. After implementing feedly into my daily routine, I can now consume double the amount of content in less time.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"https://goo.gl/XsxunU\" target=\"new\">Get our <b>State of Content Marketing report</b></a></p>\n<p>Pre-feedly, I was literally using an Excel spreadsheet to keep track of all the magazines that I was visiting weekly. I would record what site I was visiting, the day I last checked it, and the title of the last article, so I could pick up where I left off. Sound like a hassle? IT WAS!!!</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7820\" src=\"http://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm.png\" alt=\"Screen Shot 2016-03-28 at 5.38.34 PM\" width=\"1362\" height=\"744\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm.png 1362w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm-300x164.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm-768x420.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm-1024x559.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm-1200x656.png 1200w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-5-38-34-pm-800x437.png 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1362px) 100vw, 1362px\" /></p>\n<p>After being introduced to feedly, I honestly lost 10 pounds of stress. It was by far the easiest, most effective tool I use to augment my career. Not only do I follow those same magazines that I was already subscribing to, but I was exposed to countless other publications that feedly offers in my space… and now they are all in one place. Along with that, I did away with the email subscriptions, which were immensely cluttering my workflow. Not to mention, I don’t risk ever missing a single article or post, which is imperative to my profession.</p>\n<p>The typical curator goes to school to study Art History and might apprentice under a known curator until they have the skills to put on their own exhibitions.</p>\n<p>We are in a new era of digital art, though, that doesn’t require all the technical training. One has an Art History degree at their fingertips at most libraries. Many big-name curators can be followed on social media, where you can get a feel for their curation efforts.</p>\n<p>So, it ultimately comes down to getting your hands on lots of content, so that you can begin noticing trends, formulating hypotheses, and putting together thought-provoking collections.</p>\n<p>On my path to becoming a “curatorial expert,” I’m relying on feedly to feed my content needs—much like Indiana Jones relied on his whip—haha! To avoid limiting my hunger for creative ideas, I use feedly’s Collection feature to break up my content and feed into various categories: Photography, Physical Design, Graphic Design, Art News, Pop-Culture, and Visual Art. This allows me to not only keep things organized but also easily pull influences from various art mediums.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7819\" src=\"http://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1.png\" alt=\"Screen Shot 2016-03-28 at 1.23.41 AM\" width=\"1356\" height=\"641\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1.png 1356w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1-300x142.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1-768x363.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1-1024x484.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/screen-shot-2016-03-28-at-1-23-41-am1-1200x567.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1356px) 100vw, 1356px\" /></p>\n<p>Because I swim through so much content on a daily basis, it is very easy to get lost in the immensity. To augment this problem I use the tag and “save for later” features to create collections of art that work well together. I can easily communicate with my team what my thoughts are on our newest curated collection and show what influences me.</p>\n<p>With feedly, anyone with an aptitude for creativity, noticing patterns, and expressing their thoughts through creation can become a digital art curator.</p>\n<p>Contributed by Ryan Cowdrey, Director of Curation at <a href=\"http://23VIVI.com\" This database belongs to the US National Library of Medicine and is used by leading websites such as PubMed and ClinicalTrials.gov.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Asking Leo to prioritize &#8220;IL33&#8221; in any of your biopharma feeds is as simple as creating a new Topic priority and selecting &#8220;IL33&#8221; as the topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you create an &#8220;IL33&#8221; priority, Leo will be looking for <strong>all the aliases of &#8220;IL33</strong>&#8220;. leaked information from the services using their edge cache servers.</p>\n<p>Feedly uses Cloudflare as a security shield which increases the reliability and performance of the Feedly web application. As such, Cloudflare informed us it is possible that some of the Feedly Web request performed between Feb 13 and Feb 18 might have been impacted by the information leak.</p>\n<p>Despite the 1 in 3,300,000 chances of being impacted, <strong>we recommend to be extra cautious</strong> and take the following actions:</p>\n<p>1/<strong> If you are using the Feedly login/password, change your password</strong>.<strong> </strong>Go to the <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/logins\">Logins page</a> and change your password. Note: if you are using a third-party login option like Google, Facebook, or Twitter, you are NOT impacted and do not need to change your password [1].</p>\n<p>2/ <strong>Logout and log back in.</strong> On Feedly Web, click on the face bubble icon (at the top right of the screen), select the logout option and then log back in. This will invalidate your old session/cookies and create a brand new one.</p>\n<p>Our engineering team has a follow up call with the Cloudflare team later this afternoon and we will update this post if we learn anything that changes these recommendations.</p>\n<p>We want to thank the Cloudflare team for how well they handled this situation. It is how you manage exceptions that defines your brand, and Cloudflare did really well despite what might have been a very stressful moment for them. We look forward to continuing to work with them to make Feedly safer and more reliable.</p>\n<p>Please let us know if you have any questions.</p>\n<p>-Seb, David, and Edwin</p>\n<p>[1] The third party login authentication is performed via OAuth. You login directly with those 3rd party sites and Feedly only gets an authentication token. Paged Scrolling, and Pro upgrade &#8211; all on both Android and iOS.</p>\n<h2>iPad and Android Tablet</h2>\n<p>After twelve weeks of phone exploration, it is time to shift our focus to the tablet and see how some of the innovation translate to a bigger screen. In Experiment 07, we are sharing with you some ideas we have around how the iPad compact, text-only, magazine, and cards view might look like.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-24-21.17.08.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p><em>Questions for the community</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 1</strong> &#8211; Are you satisfied with how the new mobile views look on the iPad and Android Tablets?</p>\n<p><strong>Question 2</strong> &#8211; Are you satisfied by the new navigation model and the side-by-side implementation?</p>\n<p>We look forward to your feedback on the #ipad slack channel.</p>\n<h2>Power Search</h2>\n<p>Power Search is the ability for you to search for specific articles in your Feedly feeds and boards. You can think of it as a personalized search engine focusing only on the sources you trust. It is one of the top Feedly Pro features. In Experiment 07, we implemented a mobile-friendly version of the experience available on the Web.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-24-21.14.48.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like on the Web, you can use <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/find-and-filter-the-best-content-on-the-web-with-power-search/\">operators</a> (AND, OR, quotes, etc..) to refine your searches and use filters to narrow the result to the right sources, content time or popularity.</p>\n<p><em>Questions for the Pro community</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 3</strong> &#8211; Are you satisfied with the new mobile Power Search user experience? Where you able to easily find a specific article in your Feedly?</p>\n<p><strong>Question 4</strong> &#8211; Is there a feature we could add to Power Search to make it more useful to you?</p>\n<p>Please join the 07-power-search channel on Slack if you would like to discuss the Power Search feature with the product team.</p>\n<h2>Settings</h2>\n<p>As part of the continuous polish effort, we added settings support. You can now access the settings panel from the bottom of the left navigation bar and customize: the theme, the start page, the auto-mark-as-read behavior, the default view, and many more features.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-24-21.13.05.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<h2>Paged-Scrolling</h2>\n<p>The lack of paged scrolling has been one of the biggest &#8220;snakes&#8221; in the new design. About 10 % of the users seem to prefer paged scrolling to the new smooth scrolling. We decided last week to try to understand more. We created a private Slack channel with the 75 people who were not satisfied with the new smooth scrolling. Through these conversations, we learned that what users really liked about the old experience is that it made it easy to not over-scroll or under-scroll and empowered users to scroll through content faster.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple \"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-24-20.56.10.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>As part of Experiment 7, we are pushing out an idea a few users suggested: it would be nice to have a preference which would allow you to have some kind of intelligent scrolling that would automatically stop at the right place.</p>\n<p>If you go to the new settings panel, you will see a &#8220;Paged&#8221; scrolling option that should allow you to play with this idea.</p>\n<p><em>Question to the community</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 5</strong> &#8211; If you are part of the &#8220;I miss the old scrolling&#8221; camp, is this option enough to remove all the frustration caused by the lack of productivity? Let us know in the 01-scrolling channel</p>\n<h2>Upgrade to Pro</h2>\n<p>As part of Experiment 07, we now allow non-pro users to upgrade to Pro and either unlock some interesting feature or just back Feedly. To thank the Lab community, this mobile upgrade to Pro offers a free 30-day trial.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/Screenshot-2018-09-24-21.13.36.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p><em>Question to the community</em></p>\n<p><strong>Question 6</strong> &#8211; If you end up trying the upgrade experience, please let us know what you think and if there are friction points we could remove.</p>\n<p><strong>Question 7</strong> &#8211; If you are not a Pro user, please let us know if there is a feature we could add to the Pro offering to inspire you to upgrade!</p>\n<p>Please use the 08-pro Slack channel for all the Pro related conversations.</p>\n<h2>Next Three Weeks</h2>\n<p>The focus of the next 3 weeks is to finalize the iPad implementation and polish as much as we can.</p>\n<p><strong>Question 8</strong> &#8211; If you still see any gaps preventing you from using the new Lab app as your primary reading/research experience, we would love to hear about them.</p>\n<p>We would like to thank once again everyone in the Lab community for participating in this giant experiment and helping us design the best Feedly possible. Your feedback and ideas help us better understand how you use the product and how to optimize and refine our decisions.</p>\n<p>-Edwin, Petr, and Emily</p>\n<p>Love the Web? rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>There are some common questions about the “send now” feature for team newsletters. Here is a quick reference to guide you through the steps.</p>\n<p>Sending newsletters on demand makes it easy to grab a snapshot of your team boards and feeds. We want to help your team move forward and save time!</p>\n<p>Time is of the essence, so let’s review the steps and jump into your questions!</p>\n<h2>How To Send Now:</h2>\n<ol>\n<li>Save new articles to your board (Nothing saved since the last email, the board won’t send now)</li>\n<li>Open your <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/team/newsletters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Newsletter dashboard</a></li>\n<li>Select the board or feed to send now</li>\n<li>Click send now</li>\n</ol>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/09/send-now.png\" /><figcaption>Newsletters are proving to be a useful tool for team collaboration.<br />\nOur teams use them internally, and we will keep building with your feedback in mind.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Thank you to all the teams who have sent questions, feedback, and bug reports!</p>\n<h2>FAQs</h2>\n<p><strong>Why didn’t I receive my newsletter? Common problems &#38; solutions:</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>No new articles saved since the last newsletter sent. It will only send if there are new articles available (ie. saved) in the board.</li>\n<li><strong>Solution:</strong> For now, we suggest removing and then re-saving some articles to the board. After that, return to the <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/team/newsletters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">newsletter dashboard</a> and hit “send now” once again.</li>\n<li>It works the same way the very first time you activate a newsletter and for your future scheduled newsletters.</li>\n<li>Maybe the newsletter is in spam.</li>\n<li><strong>Solution:</strong> Please check your spam folder and add <strong>&#60;teams@feedly.com&#62;</strong> to your address book. That will tell your email provider to deliver newsletters to your inbox.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>What articles will (or won’t) be included in the newsletter when I hit Send Now?</strong></p>\n<p>On-demand newsletters only include new articles saved since the last newsletter sent. This is the most common reason why a newsletter doesn’t send.</p>\n<p>To send an on-demand newsletter with specific articles, we suggest removing and then re-saving those articles to the board. After that, return to the <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/team/newsletters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">newsletter dashboard</a> and hit “send now” once again.</p>\n<p><strong>What about analytics?</strong></p>\n<p>Coming soon <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f642.png\" alt=\"🙂\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /></p>\n<p><strong>How do I add newsletters to my Feedly account?</strong></p>\n<p>We suggest starting a <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=blog&#38;utm_medium=launch&#38;utm_campaign=on-demand-newsletter\">30-day free trial</a> of Feedly Teams. href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2F6-ways-to-distribute-content%2F&#38;linkname=Give%20your%20content%20distribution%20wings\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2F6-ways-to-distribute-content%2F&#38;linkname=Give%20your%20content%20distribution%20wings\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2F6-ways-to-distribute-content%2F&#38;linkname=Give%20your%20content%20distribution%20wings\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>If a tree falls in a forest and no one hears it, does it make a sound? If you create a piece of content, but no one reads it, does it exist?</p>\n<p>Despite investing time, money, and sweat into creating the content, driving readers to your content can be just as difficult. Whether you are a content marketer, a blogger, or a big publisher, this has becoming increasingly difficult in an accelerating world of online content and biased social feeds. In our &#8220;<a href=\"https://goo.gl/XsxunU\" target=\"_blank\">State of Content Marketing</a>&#8221; report, one in five marketers reported distribution as a top challenge.</p>\n<p>So just how do you distribute content these days?</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"https://goo.gl/XsxunU\" target=\"new\">Get our <b>State of Content Marketing report</b></a></p>\n<p>We went to three companies with thriving content marketing strategies—Buffer, Help Scout, and InVision—and asked them about their distribution strategies.</p>\n<p>Here are seven ways to distribute your content.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7681\"></span></p>\n<h2>1. Social</h2>\n<p>Despite recent conversations that it has become increasingly important to earn attention on social media because of the changing algorithms that encourage brands and publishers to use paid social ads, brands are continuing to use social as a primary channel for content distribution. “Social traffic is definitely down for us,” says Kevan Lee, content crafter at Buffer. “At the same time, it’s our second biggest referrer source. Still we get about 100k or so a month from social. That one is definitely significant.”</p>\n<h2>2. SEO</h2>\n<p>Sure, SEO is a long play that can take months to deliver benefits. But over time it can become the gift that keeps on giving. Forward-thinking blogs still report that SEO is key to their audience traffic. For some, this is a deliberate strategy that they have invest in over time. For others, it has been a product of a bigger commitment to quality content.</p>\n<p>Buffer has seen tons of traffic originating from search. “Having written the longer form content and writing it focused on specific topics has been a good strategy—though I’m not sure if I’d call it a strategy,” says Lee. “I’m not sure if we set out to do it necessarily but it ended up working out that way.”</p>\n<h2>3. Social Ads</h2>\n<p>In recent months, the feed algorithms at major social networks have continued to morph, making it harder for business content to stand out without the help of paid social ads. It takes some experimenting with your content and audience—and some mulah—but social ads is another way to increase the reach of your content.</p>\n<p>InVision spends about $4000 per month on content promotion various social media channels, including Linkedin, Facebook, Twitter, and other industry-specific outlets like Dribbble, according to head of content at InVision, Clair Byrd. “It’s not a lot of money,” she says, “but it’s enough to understand what content works best and it helps us create more things that work best.</p>\n<h2>4. Email</h2>\n<p>Growing an email list for content is a great way to ensure that the people who are interested in your content are getting it sent straight to their email inbox.</p>\n<p>Buffer, for instance, has a list of 45k which it uses for distribution.</p>\n<p>InVision says that email is still its most powerful channel and does one overall content email a week—a piece of content that performs strongly. “They’re free, and they tell us a lot about what’s working,” says Byrd.</p>\n<p>InVision also send out a stand alone email for key content initiatives, depending on how bit the impact is for the company.</p>\n<p>“We run content like people run product,” says Byrd. “Everything is campaign based, and everything we can tear apart. So if we think that a release is going to be Tier 1, we will support the content just like the Tier 1 product.</p>\n<h2>5. Partnerships</h2>\n<p>Syndication partnerships with other blogs or publications are another way to engage a large audience that goes beyond your user population. “One of our main distribution channels that runs almost automatically is our partnership with the Huffington Post,” says Gregory Ciotti, content strategist at Help Scout. “We set up agreements with them and Business Insider. They’ll handpick something they want to run. We just require that they use real canonical tags to protect our search. They offer us a small byline that links back to HelpScout. So all of those are happening automatically. People  will overestimate how much traffic is sends back, but either way, it is helpful. Syndication is definitely fantastic.”</p>\n<h2>6. Content Submission Sites</h2>\n<p>There are many sites for communities to post interesting and relevant content. Dribbble, Quibb, and Reddit are just a few examples. For some content distribution strategies, it may make sense to participate in the conversations at these sites and to submit content in a way that helps the community.</p>\n<p>The key, of course, is to respect the site for what it is—a community—and to avoid spamming by truly becoming a part of it and taking part in the conversations.</p>\n<h2>7. Sponsored Content</h2>\n<p>Many brands are increasingly using sponsored content services, or native ad platforms, like Outbrain and Taboola. These services try to reach more people placing your content within online publications that reach a relevant audience or post about similar things. In addition to distribution, it can provide a method of testing the efficacy or your content among a known persona or help you explore what persona reacts well to your content.</p>\n<p>These are our experts’ six recommendations. What do you use to reach more people with your content?</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"https://goo.gl/XsxunU\" target=\"new\">Get our <b>State of Content Marketing report</b></a></p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n           ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 15 Mar 2016 14:00:21 href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ftrend-report-the-rise-of-live-video-streaming%2F&#38;linkname=Trend%20Report%3A%20The%20Rise%20of%20Live%20Video%20Streaming\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><h2>The Trend: Live Video Streaming</h2>\n<p>In our increasingly digital and visual world, businesses across industries are fighting attention amidst the noise. Video as a medium has become one of the most effective ways to stand out and connect with an audience. Video quickly conveys meaning and emotion. It’s memorable, and it catches the eye in a sea of text and static images.</p>\n<p>To hit home the growing popularity of video: Over one billion people use Youtube (that’s almost one third of all people on the internet), and the number of daily Youtube viewers has increased 40 percent since March 2014.</p>\n<p>Accordingly, many social media sites like Twitter, Instagram, and Facebook have integrated some form of video content on their platforms. Additionally, new social media platforms have recently emerged that feature video as the central medium for interaction.</p>\n<p>More and more, brands are recognizing the value of video as an online marketing strategy. <a href=\"http://www.demandmetric.com/content/video-marketing-benchmark-report-0\" target=\"_blank\">Demand Metric</a> completed a survey of 398 marketing, sales, and business professionals which revealed that 69 percent have used video marketing and another 31 percent are planning to. A recent study of 200 executives by <a href=\"https://www.yourbrandlive.com/press/new-research-reveals-power-of-live-streaming-video-for-brands\" target=\"_blank\">Brandlive</a> found that 44 percent held a live streaming event in 2015 and 39 percent believe live streaming video will be important to their marketing efforts going forward.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"callforaction\" href=\"https://goo.gl/TQj0XN\" target=\"new\">Learn more about Social Selling and feedly</a></p>\n<p>The video trend is growing alongside the surging smartphone use trend, as more and more people use phone cameras. Daily mobile internet usage continues to grow year by year, on a global scale. Of all mobile traffic, online video now accounts for upwards of 50 percent.</p>\n<p>The prevalence of both video and smartphones have paved the way for newer social platforms centered around live streaming video, like Periscope, Meerkat, and now Blab.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7873\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://blab.im/\" target=\"_blank\">Blab.im</a> (which is still in beta) is quickly growing in popularity. As a platform that is truly social, interactive, informational, and fun, Blab is certainly worth getting acquainted with for its many potential uses as a tool for business and marketing.</p>\n<p>Since Blab is one of the newest of the live video trend, let&#8217;s take a closer look.</p>\n<h2>What Is Blab?</h2>\n<p><a href=\"http://Blab.im\" target=\"_blank\">Blab.im</a> is a live video broadcasting platform for hosting, watching, and joining conversations.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_7891\" style=\"width: 793px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-7891\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-7891 size-full\" src=\"http://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/screen-shot-2016-04-04-at-4-35-45-pm.png\" alt=\"Screen Shot 2016-04-04 at 4.35.45 PM\" width=\"783\" height=\"522\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/screen-shot-2016-04-04-at-4-35-45-pm.png 783w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/screen-shot-2016-04-04-at-4-35-45-pm-300x200.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/screen-shot-2016-04-04-at-4-35-45-pm-768x512.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 783px) 100vw, 783px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-7891\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">THis is a caption</p></div></p>\n<p>Image source: https://blab.im/about</p>\n<p>While many have likened it to &#8220;Periscope for groups,” you can also think of it as a cross between a talk show and a webinar. It can be used for either of those things as well as casual hang outs, debates, discussions, and workshops. There is nothing quite like it on the market, although it incorporates the best components of several different social media platforms.</p>\n<p>Anyone can host their own Blab. It’s available for anyone to watch and interact with. No professional equipment is necessary.</p>\n<p>Blab supports two to four “presenters&#8221; at a time, displayed in a grid, à la Brady Bunch. Meanwhile, other participants can watch the conversation live on video while adding to the discussion and posing questions via text chat. The host can even pull in audience members into the “hot seat” on the live video chat from time to time, if they so choose.</p>\n<p>After the chat wraps up, the conversation can be re-watched on Blab, and the hosts have the option to post the recording to Youtube or embed it on their own site.</p>\n<h2>Industry</h2>\n<p>Blab.im primarily seems to be used by solopreneurs and online thought leaders, discussing topics that range from sports to politics to social media trends.</p>\n<p>Blab is also ripe for online marketers and sales departments in just about any industry. It’s ideal for brands that want to give their customers a chance to interact in a personal way, visually demonstrate the value of their product or service, or establish their brand&#8217;s expertise and thought leadership. Granted, a direct sales pitch or advertisement won’t fly on this platform. But the interactive and visual nature of Blab opens doors to a number of benefits for businesses.</p>\n<h2>Why Blab Could Change Your Business</h2>\n<p>Blab can be used for a number of valuable business functions. It shortens the distance between you and your customer and opens up a new realm of in-the-moment experiences to create. From an online marketing standpoint, it’s a great platform for developing authentic and personalized connections with clients because it is live and unpolished. Showing, rather than just telling, and being able to answer customer concerns on the spot goes a long way in developing trust and loyalty.</p>\n<p>Here are some examples of a variety of ways Blab can be used for business:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Unveil new products with live demonstrations.</li>\n<li>Provide group coaching sessions.</li>\n<li>Conduct a Q&#38;A session or office hours.</li>\n<li>Demonstrate expertise by providing useful info for your audience.</li>\n<li>Demonstrate transparency by answering tough customer questions.</li>\n<li>Discuss strategy with your peers.</li>\n<li>Give a behind-the-scenes experience to your tribe.</li>\n<li>Network with your target audience by being a participant in other shows.</li>\n<li>Brainstorm ideas with your audience, almost like a focus group.</li>\n<li>Get feedback on changes you’ve implemented or ideas you’re considering.</li>\n<li>Record and re-use a Blab conversation as a podcast or blog post.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Learn More</h2>\n<p>Blab.im is still in beta, so the best way to get acquainted with it is to watch shows by folks who have proven success on the platform. Here are a few to get you started:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://blab.im/bryankramer\" target=\"_blank\">Bryan Kramer</a> &#8211; CEO of PureMatter</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://blab.im/kimgarst\" target=\"_blank\">Kim Garst</a> &#8211; Social selling strategist</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://blab.im/iSocialFanz\" target=\"_blank\">Brian Fanzo</a> &#8211; Digital live streaming strategist</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Now is the perfect time to jump on Blab and increase your brand’s visibility while the competition is slim. Check out their Getting Started on Blab post to learn more.</p>\n<p>Posted by <a href=\"http://intentionaltravelers.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Michelle Chang</a>, feedly Contributor</p>\n<p 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"Introduction to Leo 0.5","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=11707","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div        <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fintroduction-to-leo-0-5%2F&#38;linkname=Introduction%20to%20Leo%200.5\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fintroduction-to-leo-0-5%2F&#38;linkname=Introduction%20to%20Leo%200.5\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fintroduction-to-leo-0-5%2F&#38;linkname=Introduction%20to%20Leo%200.5\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow
