target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>Sometimes you want to follow high volume publications like The Verge, NY Times, or VentureBeat because you trust them, but you are only interested in narrower topics, trends, or mentions.<br></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Reducing noise and information overload is a problem we care passionately about. We have been working over the last 12 months on a new feature called Leo. You can think of Leo as&#160;<a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo/\">your non-black-box research assistant</a>&#160;– an easy-to-control AI tool which helps you reduce noise in your feeds and never miss important articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions leoAction\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/Q6ONey\" class=\"button accent\">Join leo beta</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Here is a quick overview of the Leo 0.5 Beta feature set.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>New Priority Tab</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are part of the Leo 0.5 Beta Program, each of your feeds has now 2 tabs. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-00.54.59.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>The All Tab includes all the articles published by the sources you follow.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The new Priority Tab includes the subset of articles flagged by Leo as important &#8211; based on the priorities you defined for your Leo.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Three Core Prioritization Skills: Mentions, Topics, and Like Board</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo 0.5 ships with three core skills: mentions, topics, and like-<g class=\"gr_ gr_4 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Grammar only-ins doubleReplace replaceWithoutSep\" id=\"4\" data-gr-id=\"4\">board</g>. Each of these skills <g class=\"gr_ gr_5 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Grammar multiReplace\" id=\"5\" data-gr-id=\"5\">allow</g> you to prioritize articles differently.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-00.55.35.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo 0.5 ships with three core prioritization skills</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>The <strong>mentions skill</strong> allows you to prioritize articles based on mentions of people, company or keywords which are important to you.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-00.56.07.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Ask Leo to prioritize articles mentioning JP Morgan</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, you can ask Leo to prioritize all the articles that mention &#8220;JP Morgan&#8221;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The<strong> topic <g class=\"gr_ gr_5 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Style multiReplace\" id=\"5\" data-gr-id=\"5\">skill </g></strong><g class=\"gr_ gr_5 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_disable_anim_appear Style multiReplace\" id=\"5\" data-gr-id=\"5\"> <g class=\"gr_ gr_4 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Grammar multiReplace\" id=\"4\" data-gr-id=\"4\">allow</g></g> you to prioritize articles which are about a specific topic you are interested&#160;in.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-00.56.20.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Ask Leo to prioritize articles about quantum computing</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, you can ask Leo to analyze your tech feed and prioritize articles which are about artificial intelligence, quantum computing, or gaming.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo ships with one thousand pre-trained topics. If the topic you are interested in is part of that list, the topic skill is a powerful tool to let you focus your feed on what really matters to you.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Sometimes, the topic you are interested in a very niche. This is where the <strong>Like Board skill</strong> is very useful and powerful.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-01.04.52.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Prioritize articles similar to the ones saved in your Smart Venue board</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, if you are in the Sports industry, you might be interested in the emerging Smart Venue trend. Leo does not know out of the box about Smart Venue but if you can create a board and save 30-50 articles about Smart Venue, you can use the <strong>Like Board skill </strong>to teach your Leo a new personalized topic and ask Leo to prioritize future articles which are similar to the ones you save in that board.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Once you have defined the priorities of your Leo, he will continuously read your feed and flag articles which are aligned with those priorities.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Like Board is particularly powerful because the more articles you save to that board, the more accurate Leo&#8217;s recommendation will become.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Finally, you can easily define more sophisticated priorities by combining multiple skills/layers.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-00.58.02.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Combine multiple layers</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Feedback Loop Via Less Like This</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>When Leo makes a back prioritization, you have the control to provide him feedback via the Less Like This button.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-01.05.08.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Provide Leo feedback via Less Like This</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>There are 5 different classes of feedback you can offer to your Leo:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>The &#8220;Not About&#8221; feedback allows you to teach Leo that it matched the wrong keyword or topic. For example, you were interested in ICO (Initial Coin Offering) and Leo detected ICO (Internet Commissioner Office).</li><li>The &#8220;duplicated article&#8221; feedback <g class=\"gr_ gr_20 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Grammar multiReplace\" id=\"20\" data-gr-id=\"20\">allow</g> you to flag articles which are on topic but you have already read about via a different source</li><li>The &#8220;I&#8217;m not interested in&#8221; feedback allow you to flag class of articles you are not interested <g class=\"gr_ gr_19 gr-alert gr_gramm gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim Grammar multiReplace\" id=\"19\" data-gr-id=\"19\">about</g>. For example, you might not be interested in market research type articles. If you can flag 10-20 articles as I am not interested in market research, Leo is going to learn and start prioritizing fewer market research articles.</li><li>Sometimes (<g class=\"gr_ gr_16 gr-alert gr_spell gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim ContextualSpelling multiReplace\" id=\"16\" data-gr-id=\"16\">specially</g> for keyword alerts), you might get articles from sources you do not care about. The &#8216;mute domain&#8217; feedback allows you to train your Leo to mute articles from those domains.</li><li>Finally, sometimes, the reason is more complex. The &#8216;Something else&#8217; feedback offers you an easy way out.</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<h2>Deduplication</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We also heard from a lot of users that duplicate articles are a big source of noise and echo in their feeds. If you are tired of seeing the same article or press release being pushed across multiple sources, Leo 0.5 near exact deduplication is here to help.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-02.10.19.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>A sign at the bottom right shows the count of duplicates which are automatically removed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo continuously monitors your feeds and when he detects duplicates, it automatically clean up your feeds so that you only get one copy of the article or press release.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is particularly useful if you follow a lot of Google Keyword Alerts or if you follow source that cross post content.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Control and Transparency</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>A very important aspect of the Leo promise is that it is a fun, non-black-box AI you fully control and can easily collaborate with.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-01.05.28.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Transparency via clear explanations</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Transparent because each time Leo makes a prioritization, he will explain why the article was prioritized and give you the opportunity to refine that prioritization.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-06-01.05.49.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Full control</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Control because you explicitly define all the priorities of your Leo and you can at anytime go in the Train Leo section and remove or refine a priority. No black box. No lag.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Goodbye Information Overload</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo 0.1 Alpha customers saw 40-70% noise reduction on their feeds. More targeted feeds mean that you can save time while reducing the risk of missing important articles, or being the last to know about an important risk or market opportunity.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We look forward to seeing how your will be training your Leo!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions leoAction\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span Everything is discussed openly. Every member of the team has high autonomy and can have high impact at many levels of the product and company culture.</li>\n<li><strong>We take care of our team.</strong> We provide competitive salaries, very generous stock option packages, and a full slate of benefits including health coverage and pre-tax commuter benefits. We also believe in work/life balance: we are in this for the long term.</li>\n<li>We have a flexible vacation policy, sponsor sports packages, and provide a monthly book allowance to encourage personal growth. Perks include the best equipment available on the market to help you get your job done. We pride ourselves on company get-togethers like our weekly lunches and our monthly Roadmap meetings, which reinforce <strong>our culture of collaboration and connectivity</strong>.</li>\n<li>We have offices in Palo Alto and San Francisco to help <strong>optimize teamwork while minimizing commute</strong>.</li>\n</ul>\n<h4><strong>You are:</strong></h4>\n<ul>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You have <strong>a growth mindset</strong> and love to continuously learn and grow.</span></li>\n<li>You are <strong>patient, empathic and enjoy interacting with customers</strong>.</li>\n<li>You are <strong>persistent and energetic</strong> and ready to do whatever it takes to help customers troubleshoot issues.</li>\n<li>You are <strong>a team player</strong> and enjoy working with the product team to learn how products work and offer feedback on how to improve the experience.</li>\n<li>You enjoy sharing knowledge and information with others, writing tutorials and FAQ articles.</li>\n<li>You either live in the San Francisco area or are interested in a remote working experience.</li>\n</ul>\n<h4><strong>During your first year at feedly you will:</strong></h4>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Help thousands of interesting users</strong>. The feedly community is very diverse and comes from all over the world. <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                      <img class=\"webfeeds-header__illustration webfeedsFeaturedVisual\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/trend-acceleration.jpeg\" width=\"3300\" height=\"2049\" />                                        <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                                      </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ftrend-acceleration-ideas-are-moving-faster-and-faster-can-we-keep-up%2F&#38;linkname=It%E2%80%99s%20Not%20Just%20You%3A%20Trends%20Are%20Moving%20Faster%20Than%20Ever\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ftrend-acceleration-ideas-are-moving-faster-and-faster-can-we-keep-up%2F&#38;linkname=It%E2%80%99s%20Not%20Just%20You%3A%20Trends%20Are%20Moving%20Faster%20Than%20Ever\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ftrend-acceleration-ideas-are-moving-faster-and-faster-can-we-keep-up%2F&#38;linkname=It%E2%80%99s%20Not%20Just%20You%3A%20Trends%20Are%20Moving%20Faster%20Than%20Ever\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Ftrend-acceleration-ideas-are-moving-faster-and-faster-can-we-keep-up%2F&#38;linkname=It%E2%80%99s%20Not%20Just%20You%3A%20Trends%20Are%20Moving%20Faster%20Than%20Ever\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>Some people are calling it Content Shock or Content Clutter. We like to call it the Content Renaissance.</p>\n<p>Whatever you call it, many of us have been talking about the same idea: Content is coming to us at an ever increasing rate.</p>\n<p>The result is that ideas, trends, and memes have become a swiftly moving current that will easily overwhelm us or leave us behind if we let it.</p>\n<h2>The Content Renaissance Is Creating an Explosion of Content</h2>\n<p>We live in an unprecedented age in which we are creating more content than ever before and in which we have more access to information and ideas than ever.</p>\n<p>Ninety percent of the world’s data has been generated in the last two years, according to one <a href=\"http://www.sciencedaily.com/releases/2013/05/130522085217.htm\" target=\"_blank\">study</a>. Google publishes 20 petabytes of information every day, according to <a href=\"https://www.promodo.com/blog/amazing-google-facts-you-most-probably-didnt-know/\" target=\"_blank\">Promodo</a> in 2013. To put it in perspective, there have been 5,000 petabytes of information created from the dawn of civilization to 2003. In 2014, WordPress reported that it was publishing 17 posts every second—or 1.5 million posts per day. In that year alone, 72 million websites were created.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7630\"></span></p>\n<p>And the production of content is still growing. Ninety-two percent of marketers are creating more digital content now than they did two years ago, and 83 percent expect this number to continue to rise, according to <a href=\"http://www.komarketingassociates.com/industry-news/report-marketing-professionals-see-a-dramatic-rise-in-content-production-2939/\" target=\"_blank\">Accenture</a>.</p>\n<p>If this isn’t overwhelming enough, social networks are accelerating this flow of information still faster. According to <a href=\"https://www.domo.com/blog/2014/04/data-never-sleeps-2-0/\" target=\"_blank\">Domo</a>, every minute:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Facebook users share almost 2.5 million posts</li>\n<li>Twitter users tweet almost 300,000 times</li>\n<li>Instagrammers upload almost 220,000 photos</li>\n</ul>\n<p>This influx of content carries plenty of upside for individuals and publishers alike. It’s easier than ever to share your gospel. Creatives thrive in this new medium, and businesses are creating engaging new experiences.</p>\n<p>However as consumers of this content and as merchants of ideas, the firehose is overwhelming as it is satisfying.</p>\n<h2>Enter Trend Acceleration</h2>\n<p>The result of the Content Renaissance is that content has become the currency of change. Ideas are being exchanged, embraced, and evolved at an ever increasing rate.</p>\n<p>As a result, while trends used to come and go over the span of years, these days discussions are moving thought leadership at a cadence of months or weeks.</p>\n<p>This deeply impacts the way we do business and the way we operate in this world.</p>\n<p>For marketers, in particular, it means that the ability to engage consumers with fresh and relevant points of view is a swiftly moving window. The current of new ideas is so fast, that it is easier than ever to attach your brand to something considered more passé.</p>\n<p>For PR people, it means a bigger challenge in cutting through the noise with something sharply unique.</p>\n<p>For corporations, it means creating products that serve customers in a quickly changing competitive landscape. Small businesses have to move just as quickly with often times fewer resources.</p>\n<p>So how do you stay ahead of it?</p>\n<p>The key is to identify the right <strong>signals</strong> and then implement the right workflow to <strong>monitor</strong> those signals.</p>\n<p><strong>1.Recognize the need to monitor for yourself and your company, and dedicate resources to the task.</strong></p>\n<p>Monitoring is an art, science, and a process, and above all, it takes time and attention. Recognize that with your daily work or within your business and be deliberate about setting aside time for yourself or people resources within your business to do it well. Have you set aside some time for yourself to crunch through these trends? Do you have the right people on the job? Do you have the right tools in place?</p>\n<p><strong>2. Identify the right signals — create the right mix of places and people to follow.</strong></p>\n<p>Many algorithms today try to guess what is important to us by predicting future interests based on past behavior. Staying on the cusp, however, requires a proactive, but efficient, way of identifying what the right signals are. A signal is that place from which new ideas and new trends are broadcast.</p>\n<p>Identify the most important pieces of news or thinking on the new trend and use those to develop a <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/get-the-right-content-on-your-feedly/\">personalized content mix</a> based on:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Key influencers and thought leaders</strong> &#8211; Who are the main voices in the articles? Who are the main people they cite? Who are other thinkers in that realm?</li>\n<li><strong>Key producers in Twitter, YouTube, Facebook, and Reddit</strong> &#8211; Real-time channels can indicate the earliest rumblings of a trend. Find the right people in each of these social networks and add them to your list. <a href=\"http://storyful.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Storyful</a>, a company that specializes in newsgathering from social networks, recommends finding relevant content from each of these social channels to get a full picture.</li>\n<li><strong>Specific Geographies to keep a pulse on</strong> &#8211; Is your main industry magazines in New York? Is it a new irrigation system being tried in Venice? Is it human trafficking legislation in San Diego? Consider some local sources in your content mix.</li>\n<li><strong>Keywords</strong> &#8211; Are there buzzwords that show up within the trend you are monitoring? If you are following the Tea Party movement in America, should you be following any mentions of “Sarah Palin,” “immigration,” “gun ownership”?</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Here are some great feeds that other people have created to follow the latest trends in a given industry:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Sarah Levine and the most important publications in <a href=\"http://feedly.com/sarahmakesmaps/maps\" target=\"_blank\">Maps</a>.</li>\n<li>Guy Kawasaki’s Collection of <a href=\"http://feedly.com/GuyKawasaki/Social%20Media%20Marketing\" target=\"_blank\">Social Media sources</a>.</li>\n<li>Rand Fishkin’s Collection on <a href=\"http://feedly.com/randfish/Inbound%20Marketing\" target=\"_blank\">Inbound Marketing</a>.</li>\n<li>Ann Handley’s Collection on <a href=\"http://feedly.com/MarketingProfs/Content%20Marketing\" target=\"_blank\">Content Marketing</a>.</li>\n<li>Hilah Johnson’s Collection on <a href=\"http://feedly.com/HilahCooking/Food%20YouTube%20Channels\" target=\"_blank\">Food YouTube Channels</a>.</li>\n<li>Annie Cushing’s Collection on <a href=\"http://feedly.com/annie/Analytics\" target=\"_blank\">Data Analytics</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>3. Centralize these signals into the fewest number of places that allow you to follow these people, publications, and trends most efficiently.</strong></p>\n<p>Much of today’s content is on different platforms and requires you to go to it. Flip this around and have this content come to you by creating the right workflow. Focusing in on the workflow will allow you to crunch through the onslaught of content quickly and methodically. We’re a bit biased, but naturally we recommend Feedly as a place for you to house all the blogs, publications, Google Alerts, YouTube feeds, Facebook feeds, and Twitter feeds you are monitoring.</p>\n<p>With Feedly, you can create a separate feed for each specific trend, vertical, product, or industry that you are monitoring. With <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/\">Feedly Pro</a>, you can even use <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/find-and-filter-the-best-content-on-the-web-with-power-search/\">Power Search</a> to search for specific terms within a feed, organized by media type or date.</p>\n<p><strong>4. Archive the data points.</strong></p>\n<p>Create a methodology for saving and organizing the precious content pieces you find online that speak to the topic you are following. Many people like to use Evernote or Pocket to save articles. We highly recommend using boards within Feedly to save and organize the great pieces of content you want to share with others or return to later.</p>\n<p><strong>5. More eyes, better vision: Crowdsource monitoring</strong></p>\n<p>The more people who are collaborating together, the better a pulse you will have on trends and the richer your conversations will be around them. Create an internal system through which all employees can contribute important content on new trends and key teams can ingest this information in an organized fashion.</p>\n<p><strong>6. Broadcast your interest and join the conversation</strong></p>\n<p>The more you can show your interest in a particular conversation the easier it will be to have conversations with the right influencers. Consider taking the content you are monitoring and broadcasting your interest in the vertical via social channels.</p>\n<p>What are ways that you and your company have found effective in finding the right signals or organizing them into workflows that are easy to follow?</p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n           ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 10 Mar 2016 15:00:40 +0000","feedId":887,"bgimg":"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/trend-acceleration.jpeg","linkMd5":"f9df96dba603d00529d8732061aedb98","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn3@2020_4/2020/08/16/13-38-37-038_ffb251383d6955ae.webp","destWidth":3300,"destHeight":2049,"author":"feedly","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/trend-acceleration.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn81@2020_3/2020/08/16/13-38-53-719_ffb251383d6955ae.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Forganize%2F&#38;linkname=Design%20Review%3A%20The%20New%20Organize%20Experience\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Forganize%2F&#38;linkname=Design%20Review%3A%20The%20New%20Organize%20Experience\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Forganize%2F&#38;linkname=Design%20Review%3A%20The%20New%20Organize%20Experience\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p><strong>Update:</strong> We launched the new organize experience! <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/organize-sources/\">Read the announcement here</a>.</p>\n<p>At Feedly we&#8217;re focused on simplifying how you consume information every day. We help you find and connect to all the sources you need. The next step is giving you a simple, effective way to organize your sources by topic, project, industry, client, or passion.</p>\n<p>Being able to re-organize these sources as your needs evolve is a critical part of controlling the signal-to-noise ratio in your Feedly. One of our goals for 2017 is to make re-organizing sources easier, faster, and more data-driven.</p>\n<p>We started this journey by reaching out to the community and listening to your feedback. <strong>Thank you</strong> to the 27,000+ people who participated in the Organize survey by telling us how we could improve the experience. Here are some of the most popular requests from the survey:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Visibility into broken sources and publishing frequency</li>\n<li>Ability to sort and filter feeds</li>\n<li>Show personal reading statistics</li>\n<li>Editing single sources and bulk operations to move or unfollow sources</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>00 — Design Direction</h2>\n<p>Based on the survey data, we decided to center the new organize experience on 3 features:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Show a bird’s-eye view of your sources using filters for <strong>source activity</strong> (active, inactive, or unreachable) in a specific feed or by searching for a source by name</li>\n<li>Surface <strong>metadata</strong> about how useful each source has been to you recently. In the first version, we’re focusing on the number of articles per month and how many of those you have read</li>\n<li>Make it <strong>easy to act</strong> on this metadata: select multiple sources and move or unfollow them</li>\n</ol>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-browser webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/screenshot-1-1.jpg\" /></figure>\n<h2>01 — Filter sources</h2>\n<p>During our research, we found that on average people follow about 75 sources organized into 10 feeds. At the same time, some users have 20,000 sources and more than 200 feeds.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-9440 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/chart-2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1104\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/chart-2.png 1104w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/chart-2-300x185.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/chart-2-768x473.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/chart-2-1024x631.png 1024w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1104px) 100vw, 1104px\" /><br />\nOne of our challenges was finding a way to enable you to manage a large number of sources as easily as just a few. We decided on an table-like interface with a list of all your sources along with some reading statistics. This list, combined with a powerful filter, should solve two big needs expressed in your survey responses: 1) to find sources that are either unreachable or too noisy, and 2) to see which of your feeds the source belongs to.</p>\n<p>We also created some shortcuts for the most-used operations like finding unreachable or inactive sources.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/screenshot-2-2.jpg\" /><figcaption>In the new user interface, you can filter sources by activity and by the feeds they belong to.</figcaption></figure>\n<h2>02 — Reading Statistics and Source Status</h2>\n<p>The ultimate goal of the new organize UI is to help you optimize your signal-to-noise ratio. By reviewing your personal reading statistics, you can make informed decisions about the sources you follow. You will see 2 metrics to keep things simple: how often sources are updated, and how many of those updates you read.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/screenshot-3.jpg\" /></figure>\n<p>We believe these metrics are correlated. If the feed is getting hundreds of new articles and you’re reading just a few of them, this is a good indication of where the “noise” is coming from.</p>\n<h2>03 — Batch Operations</h2>\n<p>Now that you know where most of your content is coming from and how you consume it, the next step is to take action. Our gut feeling (validated by the survey data) is that the most important actions are re-organizing your sources and feeds and unfollowing inactive or unreachable sources.</p>\n<p>In the new Organize experience, it’s easy to move multiple sources at once. You can also group sources into multiple feeds. Lastly, you can unfollow multiple sources at once by selecting them and clicking “Unfollow.”</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/screenshot-4-2.jpg\" /></figure>\n<h2>Next Steps</h2>\n<p>Soon we will push these changes to everyone who signed up for early access. After the early-access period ends, we will activate the new Organize experience for all Feedly users. In the meantime, we would love to hear your feedback on this new design.</p>\n<p>Please leave us a comment below — we&#8217;ll write you back.</p>\n<p>Stay tuned!</p>\n                </div>\n title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fhelp-us-choose-your-new-organize-experience%2F&#38;linkname=Help%20us%20choose%20your%20new%20Organize%20experience\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fhelp-us-choose-your-new-organize-experience%2F&#38;linkname=Help%20us%20choose%20your%20new%20Organize%20experience\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>Feedly is the best way to ingest the content you need for work by putting your favorite feeds in an organized newsfeed. Over the past few weeks we have rethought the way you can clean up and reorganize your feedly. I worked with the feedly team to design two different concepts and would love to hear your feedback to help us build the best organized experience possible!</p>\n<p>In a recent survey with 5,000 participants, many of you showed us that you like to reorganize your feedly for two main reasons:</p>\n<p><strong>Spring cleaning<br />\n</strong>Every once in a while you need to clean up your feedly to make sure you only follow the feeds that interest you. This involves removing inactive feeds (the ones that have not published in months), removing the feeds you don’t read anymore, and promoting articles to “must-read” publications, so you don’t miss a story.</p>\n<p><strong>Reorganization<br />\n</strong>There are other times when you feel like reorganizing parts or all of your feedly. Maybe you have new interests or you want to split a topic into a few more specific topics, such as splitting your Marketing Collection into SEO and Digital Marketing Collections. All of this involves renaming Collections, moving them around and moving feeds from one Collection to another.</p>\n<p>After a few weeks of design work with these two use cases in mind, we came up with two design directions:</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7439\"></span></p>\n<h2>Concept 1: Organize At a Glance</h2>\n<p>The main idea behind this concept is that everything is available in one page with just the crucial information you need to optimize your feedly. Your collections are listed on the right and the selected Collection’s feeds appear at the center of the page. This enables you to move from Collection to Collection without switching context.</p>\n<p>You can try out this concept on InVision: https://invis.io/D567GADVZ</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7455\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design.png\" alt=\"Selected-Design\" width=\"1154\" height=\"641\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design.png 1440w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design-300x167.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design-768x427.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design-1024x569.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design-1200x667.png 1200w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/selected-design-800x444.png 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1154px) 100vw, 1154px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>View important information at a glance<br />\n</strong>With this first concept we are showing you the essential information you need when you need it, no less, no more. For instance, when looking at a Collection you will see the feeds that are Must Read and those which are inactive. It’s just enough information for you to take action with no clutter.</p>\n<p>Because your Collections are listed on the right side, you can easily navigate from one to the other rapidly.</p>\n<p><strong>Take the main actions in one click<br />\n</strong>Most actions are one click away or one drag away. Hit the cross or the star icon to remove a feed from a Collection or mark a feed as must read, respectively (see below for examples). Use drag and drop gestures to move a feed to the Collection it should belong to and re-order your Collections.</p>\n<p>_<br />\n<em>Making a feed must read</em></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-baskervillepostthumbnail wp-image-7459\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/minimal-mustread.png?w=904\" alt=\"minimal-mustread\" width=\"904\" size-baskervillepostthumbnail wp-image-7458\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/minimal-movefeed.png?w=904\" alt=\"minimal-movefeed\" width=\"904\" height=\"392\" 100vw, 904px\" /></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">_<br />\n<em>Reordering a Collection</em></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7457\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/minimal-movecollection.png\" alt=\"minimal-movecollection\" width=\"904\" height=\"392\" sizes=\"(max-width: 904px) 100vw, 904px\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2>Concept 2: Organize with Deep Site Information</h2>\n<p>This second concept takes advantage of data tables and the feedly slider. The main page displays all of your Collections. After you select a Collection we use the feedly slider to show all of the feeds it contains.</p>\n<p>This concept focuses on showing you as much information as possible in a consistent way so you can easily decide what action to take on each item.</p>\n<p>You can try out this concept on InVision: https://invis.io/ED67GAMB2</p>\n<p>_<br />\n<em><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">Concept 2: Collection list</span></em></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7461\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/advanced-intro1.png\" alt=\"advanced-intro1\" 100vw, 1154px\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><strong>See all the data you need </strong><br />\nBoth the Collection list page and the feed list slider are tables displaying all the information you need to quickly undestand where you should take action. Quickly see which Collections have the most inactive feeds and which feeds last posted a long time ago.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight:400;\">_<br />\n<em>Last posted data on feed list</em></span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7463\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/advanced-feedata.png\" alt=\"advanced-feedata\" 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 744px) 100vw, 744px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Use a consistent popup to edit your feeds<br />\n</strong>Whether you want to edit the name of a feeds, mark it as read, remove it from a Collection, move to a different one or add it to multiple Collections, a consistent dropdown menu will be there to accomplish all these tasks across the application.</p>\n<p>_<br />\n<em>Editing a feed</em></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-7464\" src=\"https://blog1.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/advanced-movingfeeds.png\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>You may know your way around our<a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/\"> Feedly Boards</a> already. They’re a place to save useful insights you’ve found in Feedly or around the web, and share them as <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/team-newsletters/\">newsletters</a> with your teammates.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But insights can come from many kinds of media, including market reports, conference brochures, presentation decks, or whitepapers packed with industry knowledge. Typically, these exist in a PDF format.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, you can <strong>save PDFs to your Feedly Boards</strong>, so nothing is left out for a deep-dive understanding of a subject.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Run</strong>-through</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s suppose you’re an analyst for JP Morgan, learning about breaking developments in financial services. Here’s how to add the PDFs you find to your Boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Say you come across a fantastic online market report. In this case, it’s all about the technologies set to disrupt financial services in the near future.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Screen-Shot-2020-03-31-at-5.19.54-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Interesting PDF report on disruption in financial services</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Copy the URL from the browser URL bar.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Then, return to your Feedly Board, choose + ADD STORY, and paste the URL.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Finance_Disruption-3.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Select +add story and past the URL of the PDF you want to save</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Feedly will extract the PDF’s title automatically from metadata or the name of the file. You can also shorten and change the title yourself.&#160; </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Screen-Shot-2020-03-31-at-4.47.19-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Feedly detects the link is a PDF</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Before you can save a story to a Board, add a summary. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Summaries show your team what they’re about to read and why it matters. They’ll also show up your Team Newsletter.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Write your own, or do as we’ve done here and copy the first paragraph of the report’s summary. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Finance_Disruption-2.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Add a summary and click on save to board</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Once you’re done, click ‘Save To Board’.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Board should now have your PDF at the top. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Finance_Disruption.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>The PDF link has been successfully added to your board</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>It’ll stay there for anyone in your team to view and comment on. Add as many PDFs as you want to populate the Board, so you can easily access all the reference points you need in one place.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If your board is configured with a team newsletter or a Slack or Microsoft Teams notification, the PDF link will be automatically included and shared with your teammates.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Your turn</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Follow these steps to add slides, brochures, guides, market reports and more to your Boards. Now that you can save <em>any</em> insights you come across, you can be sure that crucial information never escapes you or your team when building a fuller picture of a topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro\" class=\"button accent\">DISCOVER FEEDLY BUSINESS</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Get more out of Feedly now with Team Newsletters when you upgrade to <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro\">our Business plan</a>. attentively.</li>\n<li>You have <strong>great communication skills</strong> (native English speaker or equivalent), and you enjoy giving presentations and talking to customers.</li>\n<li>You are <strong>empathetic</strong> and care deeply about the success of the customer.</li>\n<li>You are <strong>technically savvy</strong> and enjoy digging through a problem to help customers troubleshoot issues and report bugs to the development team.</li>\n<li>You are <strong>curious and coachable</strong> with a growth mindset, and you’re constantly looking to learn.</li>\n<li>You are a <strong>team player</strong> and enjoy working with the product team to learn how Feedly works and offer feedback on how to improve the experience.</li>\n<li>You either live in the San Francisco area or are interested in a remote working experience.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3>DURING YOUR FIRST YEAR:</h3>\n<ul>\n<li>You will have hundreds of conversations with customers and understand what they are trying to achieve.</li>\n<li>You will deliver passionate and engaging 1:1 demos (short, conversational, personalized to the customer’s needs)</li>\n<li>You will follow up diligently with customers to make them successful, to make sure that they are on track, and help them troubleshoot issues.</li>\n<li>You will work with our product management team to improve the end-to-end customer journey and address product gaps.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3>INTERESTED?</h3>\n<p>If you are interested in exploring this full-time opportunity, please send us some information about yourself.</p>\n<section 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"Turn Your Team Boards Into Newsletters","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=9913","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                      <img class=\"webfeeds-header__illustration webfeedsFeaturedVisual\" by client --></div>\n                                      </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fteam-newsletters%2F&#38;linkname=Turn%20Your%20Team%20Boards%20Into%20Newsletters\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fteam-newsletters%2F&#38;linkname=Turn%20Your%20Team%20Boards%20Into%20Newsletters\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fteam-newsletters%2F&#38;linkname=Turn%20Your%20Team%20Boards%20Into%20Newsletters\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fteam-newsletters%2F&#38;linkname=Turn%20Your%20Team%20Boards%20Into%20Newsletters\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>The increasing volume of information, along with accelerating industry trends, has made it harder for busy professionals and teams to keep up with emerging threats and opportunities in the market.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Current solutions for keeping up with trends fall short. By default, most teams rely on ad hoc email chains and chat to share links. These options lack context and add a lot of unwanted noise, chaos, and stress.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today, Feedly is excited to launch <strong>Team Newsletters</strong>. It&#8217;s the latest addition to <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=blog&#38;utm_medium=launch&#38;utm_campaign=team-newsletter\">our intelligence tools for teams</a>.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large webfeeds-youtube\">\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/nXQ3veDWpNI?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div></figure>\n</div>\n\n\n<p>Team newsletters are quickly becoming one of the most popular features of Feedly Teams. It is a simple yet powerful way to share important industry trends and insights with the rest of your team.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Newsletters are easy to set up and provide a quick summary of relevant articles saved by your team. And best of all, Feedly will send your newsletters to any email address, even if the person isn&#8217;t part of your Feedly Teams account.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Turn Boards Into Newsletters</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Creating a team newsletter is very easy: simply save the articles you would like to include in your newsletter to a <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/\">Team Board</a> and activate the newsletter feature on that board.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are already subscribed to <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=blog&#38;utm_medium=launch&#38;utm_campaign=team-newsletter\">Feedly Teams</a>, you can activate your newsletter in just a few clicks. Open one of your Team Boards and click on the email icon. Flip the switch to ON, and select your options. If you are new to Feedly Teams, follow the link above to&#160;try it free with your team for 30 days.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/NL-activatenewsletter-083017.gif\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Click on the email envelope icon on any of your Team Boards or Feeds to activate the newsletter feature.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Feedly will automatically convert newly saved articles into a <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/newsletter-templates/\">formatted newsletter</a> and deliver it on the schedule you choose to your teammates as well as people outside of your team. Here&#8217;s an example&#160;showing a newsletter with images turned on:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/NL-design-trends-newsletter-101917.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Newsletters are a great way to&#160;automatically send your team&#160;the latest articles saved to your Team Boards.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Team newsletters are delivered right to&#160;your&#160;inbox, giving everyone a personalized email newsletter to kick off the day.</p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"webfeeds-quote\"><p>Our strategy team uses Feedly&#8217;s newsletter feature to ensure the pertinent articles always find the team members</p><cite>Clark Cameron, 3M Strategy &#38; Market Research</cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>Among our customers using team newsletters today, we see the greatest&#160;traction&#160;from&#160;those that&#160;are focused on a single theme, project, or client. Inspired by their success, we <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/newsletter-examples/\">created&#160;4 examples of effective team newsletters</a> based on&#160;customers in finance, information security, and sales,&#160;as well as our awesome design team at Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Notes and Highlights Add Valuable Context</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can use the&#160;<a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/#notes-highlights\">notes and highlights</a>&#160;features to enrich newsletters with insights&#160;and article summaries, ask questions to spark discussion, and call your teammates&#8217; attention to important news events.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/newsletter-with-annotations.jpg\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>When you open a Team Newsletter in your inbox, you will see the&#160;<a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/#notes-highlights\">notes and highlights</a> your teammates have added to articles.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s say each person on your sales team is following a set&#160;of boards related to their target accounts. Every morning they will receive a beautiful email digest with all the new articles saved to each of the boards they follow.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>These valuable nuggets of context make it easy to scan for relevant insights to use on sales calls or strategy sessions.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>On busier days, maybe all you have time for is a 5-minute overview of what has happened related to the topics in your Team Boards. Newsletters give you just that—a quick and easy way to keep up with the latest news.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And you can always click on an item in the email to read the full article.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Flexible Scheduling and Display Options</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>In the settings for each newsletter, you can change the days and times you want your newsletters to land in your inbox.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/NL-schedulesettings-083017.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Customize each newsletter to send on your desired schedule. Choose the template with or without images.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are subscribed to two or more newsletters scheduled for the same time, Feedly will bundle them into a single email. In our team at Feedly, some of our Team Newsletters send daily, while others are less frequent. We have some newsletters scheduled for the same time, so they are combined into one email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Check out <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/newsletter-templates/\">these sample templates</a> to see examples of both display options: Text-only or with a featured image. The text-only option makes the email shorter, especially if your newsletter contains more than a few articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Include People Outside Your Feedly Team</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Easily add people outside your Feedly Team account to a newsletter too.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is popular with customers who need to send relevant updates to a wider audience such as your sales team or senior executives.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/NL-external-recipients-newsletter-102017.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Share your team newsletters with colleagues outside your Feedly Team account.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Go to your Board Settings and enter the distribution list or individual email addresses in the box labeled “external recipients.” They will receive the newsletter on the same schedule.</p>\n\n\n\n<section class=\"webfeeds-pro-tips\">If you want to send your newsletter to multiple external email addresses, be sure to use a comma to separate each email.</section>\n\n\n\n<p>External recipients—anyone not part of your Feedly Team—will be directed to the article on the source website, rather than going to the article in Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Beautiful on Any Email Client</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We have optimized Team Newsletters to be easy to read on any device and email client.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-small\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/NL-mobilegif-091117.gif\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Save Articles From Anywhere</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Using Feedly&#8217;s &#8220;<a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/support/extensions\">Save to Board</a>&#8221; browser extension, you can save articles to your boards while reading on the original source website.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/NL-browser-extension-chrome-102017.png\" alt=\"\"/><figcaption>Articles you save using the extension will appear in your newsletter the same as articles saved within Feedly.</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Ready to get started?</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=blog&#38;utm_medium=launch&#38;utm_campaign=team-newsletter\" class=\"button accent\">TRY TEAM NEWSLETTERS FOR FREE</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<h2>FAQ</h2>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: Which template should I choose?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>There are two templates available: with or without images. You can change this setting anytime. <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/newsletter-templates/\">Read more about templates</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: How do I adjust the frequency of emails?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Set a different sending schedule for each newsletter, or combine newsletters by having two or more send at the same time. Click the email envelope icon on a Team Board or Team Feed to adjust the sending days and time. For example, one board&#8217;s newsletter could send daily while all others send 2 or 3 times&#160;a week.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: What time will my newsletters&#160;arrive?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Set each board to send an email roundup at the time that&#8217;s best for your team. Select the hour of the day you want to trigger the email in each board&#8217;s settings page. The newsletter will include all of the new&#160;articles saved since the last newsletter.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Q: Why didn&#8217;t I get the newsletter?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s likely there weren&#8217;t any new articles saved to the board in the time since the last email roundup. Also confirm whether the board is set to send a roundup daily or less frequently. If you are still not receiving your newsletter,&#160;check with your email administrator to ensure you can receive emails from <em>teams@feedly.com</em>.</p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n 21:38:35","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 21:38:35","title":"What is new in Leo 0.6?","link":"https://blog.feedly.com/?p=11799","description":"\n              \n                <div>\n                  <div class=\"webfeeds-header\">\n                                                            <div class=\"webfeeds-header__title\"><!-- injected by client --></div>\n                    <div class=\"webfeeds-header__subtitle\">This is a summary of the changes we&#8217;re pushing out today as part of Leo  0.6 Beta.</div>                  </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-is-new-in-leo-0-6%2F&#38;linkname=What%20is%20new%20in%20Leo%200.6%3F\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-is-new-in-leo-0-6%2F&#38;linkname=What%20is%20new%20in%20Leo%200.6%3F\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-is-new-in-leo-0-6%2F&#38;linkname=What%20is%20new%20in%20Leo%200.6%3F\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fwhat-is-new-in-leo-0-6%2F&#38;linkname=What%20is%20new%20in%20Leo%200.6%3F\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>We pushed <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/introduction-to-leo-0-5/\">Leo 0.5</a> to a limited beta in early March and collected lots of interesting feedback. The team is listening and crunching through all that feedback and adapting Leo to improve UI/UX as well as the relevance of the underlying machine learning models.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here is a summary of the changes we&#8217;re pushing out today as part of Leo  0.6 Beta.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Smart Topics</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>One of the feedback we collected was that the difference between mentions and topics was not clear. So in 0.6, we merged these two concepts into a single one we call Smart T<g class=\"gr_ gr_56 gr-alert gr_spell gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim ContextualSpelling ins-del multiReplace\" id=\"56\" data-gr-id=\"56\">opics</g>. Just search what you want to prioritize and Leo will start analyzing the content of your feeds and prioritize the articles which are a match.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-18.17.17.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Search for companies, products, people and topics in a unified experience</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Level of Aboutness</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Sometimes you are interested in a company, product, or topic and you want to see every article mentioning that topic. Sometimes, for more popular topics, you are only interested in reading an article if the article is truly about that topic or company.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo 0.6 exposes a &#8220;level of aboutness&#8221; knob that gives you more control over the model so that you can cut out low salience matches.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-18.34.26.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Tune the aboutness parameter of each layer</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, if you are interested in NLP or BERT, you can train Leo to only prioritize research articles that are prominently about those topics (as opposed to articles which only briefly touch on those topics).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is a particularly powerful feature when combined with Google News Keyword alerts.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Global Priorities</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Some Leo 0.5 beta customers mentioned that it was critical for them to be able to define priorities that span across multiple feeds. For example, you might be doing research about Stablecoin and want to prioritize that topic across both your Tech feed, your Business feed, or all your personal or team feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In Leo 0.6, the priority designer allows you to pick &#8220;All Team Feeds&#8221; or &#8220;All Personal Feeds&#8221; as the scope of the priority.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-18.48.26.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Create a priority that spans across all your team feeds</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>This change reduces the total number of priorities you need to create and manage when researching topic and trends across multiple of your feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Quick Access</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Some users mentioned that they would like to be able to navigate their content by priority. If you are interested in a specific topic like Docker, it makes sense to be able to quickly see if there are new Docker related articles in your Feedly and easily access those articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In Leo 0.6, we added a new Priorities section to the left navigation bar that surfaces all your priorities and gives you quick access to all the article Leo has flagged as important.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-18.19.24.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Quick Access to all the NLP article prioritized by Leo</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>We added two settings in <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/account/leo\">the Leo settings</a> to let you personalize this feature. You can decide if you want to see priorities in your left navigation. If you want to see all the priorities or all the global ones (default). If you want to see all the priorities or only the ones which <g class=\"gr_ gr_6 gr-alert gr_spell gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim ContextualSpelling ins-del multiReplace\" id=\"6\" data-gr-id=\"6\">hav</g> unread articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Inlined Entities</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Your interests and priorities are continuously evolving. Often, you discover a new company, product, or topic while reading an article and you want to be able to teach Leo about it.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In Leo 0.6, the most prominent topics mentioned in an article are highlighted so that you can quickly prioritize them (or mute them)</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-19.03.35.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Inlined Entities allow for quick prioritization of new topics</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>As part of Leo&#8217;s Cyber Security skill, you will also see highlights of CVE entities. More to come soon.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Like for the Quick Access feature, there is a Leo setting that allow you to turn off Inlined Entities if that is your preference.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Like Board Improvements</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The ML team is spending time understanding how you are engaging with your priority feeds (which articles are saved to a board, which articles are being Less Like This&#8217;ed) and tuning the underlying ML models to improve accuracy. You should expect to see the quality of your priority feeds improve over the next 8 weeks.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Power Search</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>A lot of Feedly Pro and Feedly Teams customer rely on power search to find specific articles in their feeds and boards. In Leo 0.6, we are expanding power search and let you search with your priority feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/Screenshot-2019-03-19-18.22.06.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Search for BERT within the NLP priority</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For teams using Leo to discover and track trends, opportunities, and trends across industries, the combination of Leo priorities and Power search is a powerful way to quick find the most crucial information</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Thank you!</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We want to thank all the beta customers who have been working very closely with us over the last few weeks (and sometimes months). We are very grateful for your time and precious feedback. This open collaboration is not only powerful and efficient but it is also very fun. We look forward to the next 3 months!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Edwin, Remi, and Victoria</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Love reading? Love the Web? noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>The internet is a cavernous place. Opinion and insight can emerge from anywhere. Whether you’re new to Feedly or not, you want good, trusted publishers to teach you more about a certain topic, market or industry.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Feedly already digests and presents updates from the sources you value. But to really stay ahead of the curve, it pays to search beyond the publishers you already follow – to the blogs, articles, reports, and debates that are turning heads, but almost buried among the noise online.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s why we’ve given Feedly the ability to look further with <strong>Power Search across the web</strong>. It drills down into the specific information you want to find <em>beyond</em> your existing feeds and sources.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this way, you can learn something new, discover new sources for future reference and easily share reputable insights with your colleagues and social network. It intersects the exact content you’re looking for with super-specific topics and publications.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/search\" class=\"button accent\">GET POWER SEARCH</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Here’s what Power Search across the Web does, and how to use it.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Introducing Power Search across the web</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Search is a relevance game. It’s easy to lose time in the wormhole of search engines. Meanwhile, the low hit rate of typical news aggregators and alert features can leave you pulling hairs out.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Feedly gets around this with a carefully vetted database of more than 40 million trusted web sources. Collectively, they publish 110 million articles, journals, and videos. on a daily basis.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But that’s still a crazy amount of info and analysis. So we help you refine this down with buckets<strong> </strong>– categories of publications that make a search super granular.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can think of each bucket as a list of trusted publications that focus on a specific industry, function or topic. They tell the search exactly<em> </em>what to filter. You get hyper-relevant content that can be saved to a Feedly board and shared with your team or out into the wider world. Six popular buckets are surfaced automatically yet other, more narrow buckets can be chosen &#8211; we’ll show you how to do this later in our guide.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Discover what trade publications are saying about a company. Track topics on strategy sources. Bring up the conversation around a product in business magazines. The knowledge is yours to shape and tinker with.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Run-through</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Okay, let’s imagine you’re part of the Innovation Hub at Aéroports de Paris. You’re looking for ground-breaking stories and reports about the airline industry.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>First, click on the search icon to open Power Search, select the new Across the web tab, and search for the airlines topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/https___feedly_com_i_powerSearch_beyond.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Go to Power Search across the Web and search for airlines</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You get instant access to highly relevant articles from expert and trusted sources.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Screen-Shot-2020-04-01-at-11.13.46-PM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Search across the web for the topic airlines</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also search for companies, people, products, or other keywords you are interested in.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Narrow to specific publications</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The initial search is performed against a set of default buckets: strategy magazines, trade publications, business magazines, and tech blogs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But you can narrow your search to a specific slice of the web. Click on +PUBLICATIONS and lookup energy for example. This is a powerful way to find articles about airlines across a broad set of energy publications.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Airlines-in-Energy-Publication.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Search for the topic airlines in energy publications</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Refine</strong> your query with Leo topics and business events</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can refine your query by adding additional parameters (topics or business events) using the +AND operator.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, you can easily search for product launches related to the airline industry by combining the airlines smart topic and the product launch business event</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Screen-Shot-2020-04-02-at-2.15.42-AM.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Create more advanced queries with AND, OR, and Leo topics and events</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Cut through the noise with Exclude</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Okay, now let’s remove some results you 100% don’t want to find. For instance, any mention of COVID-19…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Exclude feature allows you to filter out specific topics or keywords from the search results. Click on Exclude &#62; +Topic and enter COVID-19.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Exclude-COVID.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Use the exclude feature to filter out the noise</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Advanced mode</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are a power user, you can use the Title Only knob to let Feedly know if you want to search only in the title of articles or the entire content.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The where on the web feature also includes a funnel button gives you more control over which publications should be included in the buckets. Pick leading publications if you are searching for a popular term and pick all publications if you are searching for a niche topic and you want your search to be as broad as possible.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Make your Feedly better&#160;</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Once you’ve discovered a great new article, you can click on the source name and see the other articles that the source has published.  This is a powerful way to find new sources for niche topics.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If the content is highly relevant, you can use the +FOLLOW button to add that new source to one of your Feedly feeds and receive the next articles published by that source. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/Discover-new-sources.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Use power search results to discover new insightful sources to follow</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Your turn</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>15 million users are already using Feedly for their own trade and market analysis. rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>150,000 cybersecurity professionals use Feedly to keep up with the latest security news and research insights about critical threats (vulnerabilities, malware, data breaches, threat actor groups, etc.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Cybersecurity is a game of foresight. It is a chessboard where hackers and defenders are looking to checkmate each other.<br><br>Learning more about the tactics, techniques, and procedures used by hackers can help you better prepare against them, saving you the cost and headaches that come with a breach or attack. The cost of ransomware attacks in the U.S. surpassed $7.5 billion in 2019.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But information gathering is tedious: hundreds of new articles and tweets need to be reviewed and triaged every day. Finding critical threats in that sea of information is time-consuming and overwhelming.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today, we’re excited to launch Feedly for Cybersecurity: a collection of integrations and Leo models that help you cut through the noise, break barriers between team silos, and streamline your threat intelligence.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">Try Feedly for Cybersecurity</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo is your AI research assistant.
