injected by client --></div>\n                    <div class=\"webfeeds-header__subtitle\">Train Leo to prioritize the most critical vulnerabilities in your cybersecurity feeds.</div>                  </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-and-cybersecurity%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20vulnerability%20threats\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-and-cybersecurity%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20vulnerability%20threats\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-and-cybersecurity%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20vulnerability%20threats\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-and-cybersecurity%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20vulnerability%20threats\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>Do you need to keep up with the latest vulnerabilities and threats but do not have the time to read all your security feeds? We can help.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In 2018, fifteen thousand vulnerabilities were discovered, the number of exploits doubled and more than four security articles were published every minute. Keeping up with all these trends can be time-consuming and overwhelming.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-05-21-14.01.41.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>This is a problem we are very passionate about and have been researching with two of the largest security teams in Silicon Valley. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today, we are excited to announce a new Leo skill called Security Threats.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We have been teaching Leo to read security articles and find or assess the severity of the software vulnerabilities they mention so that he can help you focus your attention on the most critical threats in your feeds first.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">TRY FEEDLY FOR CYBERSECURITY</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Here is a demo!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let&#8217;s look at how you can train your Leo to prioritize articles mentioning critical vulnerabilities related to Microsoft, WordPress, or Docker.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Cut through the noise</h2>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-06-29-14.25.34.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo reads and prioritizes the most critical threats in your feeds</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo continuously reads your feeds and short-lists the most critical vulnerabilities in the priority tab.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, you might have a cybersecurity feed connected to niche security experts, vulnerability databases, keyword alerts, etc. with thousands of new articles per month.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can train Leo to read those 1,000+ articles and prioritize the 30 or so referencing high severity threats (CVSS &#62; 8) and related to vendors you care about (Microsoft, WordPress, Docker in the example above).</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Marketing.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo&#8217;s new Security Threat skill</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>You&#8217;re in control</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo is not an opaque recommendation engine. Instead, Leo has a set of skills that gives you control over defining what information is important to you.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The new Security Threat skill allows Leo to read an article, lookup CVE, CVSS, and exploit information from multiple open source databases and determine how critical a vulnerability is.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The new Security Threat skill also includes a sophisticated machine learning model that allows Leo to assess the severity of a threat based on the vocabulary used to describe the software vulnerability. This is particularly useful for zero-day vulnerabilities which might not have a CVE or CVSS.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Training Leo to prioritize vulnerabilities is very simple.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-06-29-14.21.50.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Creating a Leo cybersecurity model</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>The first layer of the model captures the severity threshold. High means CVSS &#62; 8 or CVSS &#62; 5 but with an exploit.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The second layer of the model captures the list of vendors.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Control and transparency are core Leo design principles.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>All the articles prioritized by Leo have a green priority marker. Clicking on that marker offers an explanation of why the article was prioritized and the opportunity to refine, pause or remove that priority.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-06-29-14.58.45.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Full control and transparency</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>When an article is related to a CVE, you can also click on that CVE to get additional information about the vulnerability: description, CVSS score, exploits, patches, etc.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-06-29-15.00.47.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Quick access to CVE information</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Continuously learning and getting smarter</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo learns from his mistakes. When a recommendation is wrong, you can use the &#8220;Less-Like-This&#8221; down arrow button to correct Leo.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Screenshot-2019-06-29-15.04.55.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo learns from Less Like This feedback</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can let Leo know that he misclassified a vulnerability, miscalculated the severity, or misidentified a vendor.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo learns from your feedback and gets continuously smarter.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Streamline your open-source intelligence</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We are excited to see many security teams declutter their feeds and dig deeper into the vulnerabilities that matter to them. title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p><a href=\"http://storyful.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Storyful</a> has become a leading expert in real-time discovery, monitoring and verifying social media conversations and content. Their 200-person global team helps news organizations and brands stay on top of current events as they unfurl.</p>\n<p>“We discover and verify the content from social media using our own technology and open source technology [editor’s note: including Feedly!], monitoring the social web in real time,” explained Derek Bowler, Storyful senior journalist and special projects lead, who also helps lead the company’s internal workflows, processes, and tools.</p>\n<p>Storyful’s ability to work together across time zones and continents is central to the value that they create. They have offices in Ireland, Hong Kong, Australia, and New York. “Collaboration is at the core of Storyful,” said Bowler.</p>\n<h2>All in one place</h2>\n<p>Storyful creates a feed in Feedly for every thread they monitor, including geopolitics, cat videos, and anything else that&#8217;s important to their customers. Feedly helps Storyful&#8217;s editors follow multiple sources on the same topic without having to jump around to different sources. And when they see an influx of new articles in a feed, it often means that a new story might be breaking.</p>\n<h2>Create a diverse mix of sources with your feeds</h2>\n<p>When Storyful identifies a topic to monitor, they hand pick sources that include as many known YouTube accounts from that particular location, Facebook feeds from active posters, <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/discover/twitterFeeds\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter accounts</a>, and any relevant sub-reddits. They often include multiple content streams from each of these channels in a single feed in Feedly.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7742\"></span></p>\n<p>“That’s a one-stop shop because a lot of things we see happening in social media are encompassed in those channels,” says Bowler. “We knew a year ago that if we were monitoring those four major social platforms effectively, we were not able to monitor the topic effectively. The best thing about Feedly is that it allows you to bring it all to one place.”</p>\n<h2>Create an archive</h2>\n<p>One way Storyful uses Feedly is a bit unconventional: They use it as a YouTube archive that is easy for them to search. They have over a thousand YouTube channels to monitor. By connecting the YouTube feed to their Feedly, it becomes easy for them to know what is breaking, but also use search terms to find a specific video.</p>\n<h2>Connect Feedly with other open source tools</h2>\n<p>“There are a lot of open source tools that you can combine with Feedly to create a really powerful discovery tool for discovery desks to minimize their workflow,” Bowler says. “I no longer see Feedly as an RSS reader.”</p>\n<p>In particular, Storyful likes to use:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://fbrss.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">FB-RSS</a> &#8211; This tool creates feeds from Facebook pages.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://ifttt.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">IFTTT</a> + <a href=\"https://slack.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Slack</a> &#8211; Storyful relies on Slack for team communication. Using IFTTT, new Google Alert articles are automatically pushed to Slack via Feedly.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What do you use to monitor everyday news?</h2>\n<p>Are their tools, tips, or tricks that you or your organization use to be the first to know something? It allows us to surface notes and highlights when needed.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-image-group\">\n<figure><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/IMG_0204.png\" /></figure>\n<figure><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/IMG_0209.png\" /></figure><figcaption>The modular design creates a uniform experience</figcaption></figure>\n<h2>New Notes Feature</h2>\n<p>If you are on a Feedly <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/pro/blog-mobile-37\">Pro</a> or <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team?utm_source=feedly&#38;utm_medium=blog&#38;utm_campaign=feedly-mobile-v37\">Teams</a> plan, you can create notes to capture your thoughts and enrich articles with unique insights.                 <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-malware-threats%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20malware%20threats\" title=\"Twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fleo-understands-malware-threats%2F&#38;linkname=Leo%20understands%20malware%20threats\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p>\n<p>Cybersecurity is a game of foresight. It’s a chessboard on which attackers and defenders are constantly looking for checkmate.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Hackers launch <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.varonis.com/blog/cybersecurity-statistics/\" target=\"_blank\">a new ransomware attack every 14 seconds</a>. They’re increasingly more capable and sophisticated. Learning how they plan attacks, what techniques they use, and who they’re targeting, can make you so much better prepared. You’ll save the cost and headache of a cyber assault too. This is especially important considering that the cost of ransomware attacks in the U.S. alone surpassed $7.5 billion in 2019.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But investigating malware threats is tedious. Hundreds of new articles and tweets need to be reviewed and triaged every day. Finding critical threats in that sea of information is time-consuming and overwhelming.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We want to help you streamline your tactical and operational open-source intelligence, so that you can better protect your environment.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s why we’ve taught Leo, your <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo/\" target=\"_blank\">AI research assistant</a>, to recognize malware threats. You can ask him to read your security feeds and prioritize what’s relevant to you, your sector, and your environment.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/zTSWjL\" class=\"button accent\">try feedly for cybersecurity</a></p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s imagine that you work in a threat intelligence team and are responsible for researching and analyzing the threat landscape. You’re particularly interested in evolving malware threats (including ransomware and malvertisement).</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Cut through the noise</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You can train Leo to read your Security News feed and prioritize articles related to malware.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Malware-1.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Leo prioritizes malware articles in your Security News feed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo continuously reads the thousands of articles published in those feeds. It’s an efficient way to cut through the noise and keep up with the evolving malware landscape without the overwhelm.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>You’re in control</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo has been trained to understand broad topics like malware, as well as hundreds of specific malware types like malvertisement, ransomware, adware, bots, rootkits, spyware, etc.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Asking Leo to prioritize malware in your Security News feed is as simple as creating a new Topic priority and selecting ‘malware’ as the topic.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Malware-2.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Ask Leo to prioritize malware threats in your Security News feed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo-and-topics/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">combine topics with +AND and +OR</a> and create even more targeted priorities for Leo. For example, use +AND to focus on malware related to Android or top companies in your sector.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Malware-3.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Refine the priority to malware and Android</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also ask Leo to look for a specific type of malware like malvertisement or ransomware.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Malware-4.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Prioritize ransomware threats</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Continuously learning and getting smarter</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leo is smart. He continuously learns from your feedback. When Leo is wrong, you can use the ‘Less Like This’ down arrow button to let him know that an article he’s prioritized isn’t about malware.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Malware-5.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Let Leo know when he’s wrong</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Break down silos</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Bring your research team into the picture. They can create a Threat Intel Report Board and <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/boards/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">save the most critical insights they discover in their Feedly</a>. Then everyone with the same Board can leave notes and highlight the biggest threats.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ve seen teams create tactical and operational Boards. For instance, a Vulnerability Report can be built up with information for those that deal with security procedures, while strategic CISO Newsletters can keep management up to speed about malware and your planned response.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Articles bookmarked in a Board can be shared with the rest of the team via daily newsletters, Slack and Microsoft Teams notifications, or pushed to other apps using <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/the-feedly-cybersecurity-api/\" target=\"_blank\">the Feedly Cybersecurity API</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/break-silos.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Share the threat intelligence you collect in Feedly with other teams and apps</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Streamline your open-source intelligence</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We’re excited to see how your security team will declutter your feeds and dig deeper into the critical threats that matter to you. Leo will take care of converting the input into the right query.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Mute companies</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Curating content to share on Social Media and want to avoid mentions of your competitors?</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/Screenshot-2019-06-12-09.43.52.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Train Leo to mute mentions of SAP in your business feed</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You can train Leo to mute each of your competitors and automatically remove all the articles mentioning those competitors.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Mute people</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Want to avoid articles about specific celebrities, politicians, or executives?</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/Screenshot-2019-06-12-09.47.22.png\"/><figcaption></figcaption></figure><figcaption>Train Leo to mute mentions of Kim Kardashian</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Creating a Leo mute filter for a celebrity, politician or executive will automatically remove all the articles that mention that person from your feed.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Mute topics</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Following a broad source like TechCrunch, Wired and Forbes but do not care about topics like gaming? Less Like This</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Curious about trying Leo Mute Filters on some of your feeds? The syntax of those mute filters have changed to the v2 syntax to allow more efficient processing on the back end.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Some of the v1 mute filters using advanced queries can not be migrated to v2 will remain active as legacy filters until user delete them.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Are there limits to the number of Leo mute filters a user or team can create?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>One of the benefit of the Leo mute filters is that they can be processed more efficiently by our back-end. As a result, we are increasing the limit of Leo mute filters for Business users from 100 total to 100 per feed.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Can non-Teams user access Leo?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>We will be offering Leo to non-business users later this year via a Feedly Pro+ priced at $12/month.  You can request<strong> <a href=\"https://feedly.typeform.com/to/DW2vIZ?feature=leo-mute-filters\">early access to Pro+</a></strong> here. </p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Can a mute filter target a specific source?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>No. Mute filters can target a list of sources (what we call a feed) or all your feeds. </p>\n                </div>\n            \n\n is the article Leo is reading in the attached audio files</h3>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\"><strong>Dynamic&#160;Yield, which builds Amazon-like personalization for the rest of us, raises $38M</strong></p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">TechCrunch&#160;by Ingrid Lunden</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">Amazon, one of the world’s largest companies, has transformed the face of commerce in part because it has managed at once to be “<a href=\"https://www.amazon.co.uk/Everything-Store-Jeff-Bezos-Amazon/dp/0552167835\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Everything Store</a>” but still with a route into its sea of products that, for most users, surfaces what they might most want to see (and importantly buy or consume). That kind of personalisation has become a goal not just for e-commerce companies, but for any organization running a digital business: users are constantly distracted, and when their attention is caught, they do not want to spend time figuring out what they most want.</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">Not every business is Amazon, though, so we are seeing a crop of startups emerging that are working on ways to help the rest of the digital world be just as optimised and personalised as Amazon. Now one of them, an Israeli startup called&#160;<a href=\"http://dynamicyield.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Dynamic Yield</a>, has raised more money as it continues to expand its business, both to more platforms and to more geographies.</p>\n<p style=\"padding-left: 30px;\">The startup’s Series D has now closed off at $38 million, with the inclusion of a $5 million strategic investment from Naver, Korea’s “Google” (it’s the country’s top search portal) that is also behind messaging apps Line and Snow. The plan is for Naver to help bring&#160;<a href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/dynamic-yield\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-entity=\"dynamic-yield\" data-type=\"organization\">Dynamic Yield&#160;</a>to Korea and Japan, by incorporating its tech into its own services and those of others that work with Naver.</p>\n<p>-Olivier</p>\n by client --></div>\n                                      </div>\n                  <p><a class=\"a2a_button_facebook\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/facebook?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fnext-gen-mobile%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Next%20Generation%20Feedly%20Mobile%20Has%20Arrived\" title=\"Facebook\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_twitter\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/twitter?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fnext-gen-mobile%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Next%20Generation%20Feedly%20Mobile%20Has%20Arrived\" title=\"Twitter\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_linkedin\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/linkedin?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fnext-gen-mobile%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Next%20Generation%20Feedly%20Mobile%20Has%20Arrived\" title=\"LinkedIn\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a class=\"a2a_button_buffer\" href=\"https://www.addtoany.com/add_to/buffer?linkurl=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.feedly.com%2Fnext-gen-mobile%2F&#38;linkname=The%20Next%20Generation%20Feedly%20Mobile%20Has%20Arrived\" title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>Six months ago, we launched <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/introducing-the-mobileai-lab/\">the Feedly Lab</a> and invited 4,000 Feedly users to participate in the design and testing of the next generation of the Feedly mobile application. Today, we are excited to launch the result of that work. You can download the new app for free on the App Store and Google Play.</p>\n<section class=\"webfeeds-actions\">\n<div class=\"webfeeds-group-buttons\"><a href=\"https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/feedly-your-work-newsfeed/id396069556?mt=8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><img src=\"https://s3.feedly.com/production/head/images/apps/apple-store-badge@2x.png\" /></a><a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.devhd.feedly\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><img src=\"https://s3.feedly.com/production/head/images/apps/google-play-badge@2x.png\" /></a></div>\n</section>\n<p>Here is a quick tour of the new design.</p>\n<h2>Faster and more intuitive design</h2>\n<p>We love the Web because it is an open and distributed network that offers everyone the freedom and control to publish and follow what matters to them. The essence of this new design is to give you even more control over the information you follow and consume in your Feedly and make that experience more productive.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/new-design.gif\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Both on iOS and Android, we adopted more modern UI practices that make the experience feel lighter and easier to read. We also added more layout and density options so that user can pick the reading experience that best fits their preferences.</p>\n<h2>Powerful mark as read and save gestures</h2>\n<p>We learned from the Lab that marking as read and saving for later are key parts of our users’ workflows so we added some gestures to make those actions easier and faster to perform.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/gestures.gif\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>You can swipe left or right to trigger mark as read and save actions. You can long press to trigger a contextual menu which offers you even more actions and shortcuts.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/Screenshot-2018-12-01-14.43.09.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the global settings, you will also find an option to automatically mark stories as read as you scroll through your feeds.</p>\n<h2>Night Mode</h2>\n<p>Some of you really love to read Feedly at night, or you prefer to read in night mode all day. In the new Feedly app, we polished <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experiment-05-night-mode/\">Night Mode</a> so that you can easily read in low-light environments.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/Screenshot-2018-12-01-14.49.22.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<h2>New AI-driven discovery experience</h2>\n<p>We also love the web, because it has enabled a new generation of content creators like <a href=\"https://stratechery.com/\">Ben Thompson</a>, <a href=\"https://www.schneier.com/\">Bruce Schneier</a>, <a href=\"https://www.swiss-miss.com/\">Tina Eisenberg</a>, <a href=\"https://www.sethgodin.com/\">Seth Godin</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/\">Maria Popova</a>. These independent thinkers continuously explore the edge of the known and share insightful and inspiring ideas with their communities.</p>\n<p>Connecting people to the best sources for the topics that matter to them has been core to our mission since the very start of Feedly, but discovery is a hard problem. The web is organic, a reflection of the global community’s changing needs and priorities. There are millions of sources across thousands of topics, and we all have a different appetite when it comes to feeding our minds.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/discovery.gif\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>As part of this next generation Feedly mobile app, we are launching <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/experience-06-discovery-and-the-web/\">a new AI-driven discovery experience</a> which puts the top 50 most interesting sources across 2,000 topics at your fingertips.</p>\n<h2>Power Search</h2>\n<p>Power Search allows you to quickly find specific articles in your Feedly. This powerful search is one of the most-cited reasons for upgrading to Feedly Pro in user surveys. We are excited to bring Power Search to mobile.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/powersearch.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<h2>Notes and highlights</h2>\n<p>The new notes and highlights tools make it easy to annotate articles with your insights, save them for reference, or share them with your colleagues, friends, and followers.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/annotations.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<h2>Feedly Teams</h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team\">Feedly Teams</a> allows you to make your industry research, competitive watch, and content curation a more fun and collaborative experience. With the new Feedly mobile app, you can now access all your team feeds, team boards, newsletters, and shared annotations on your phone and tablet.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/teams.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>There are more than 7,000 teams relying on Feedly for their research and curation. We hope that the new mobile offering will inspire more users to take advantage of <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/landing/team\">the free Feedly Team 30-day trial</a>.</p>\n<h2>New Pocket integration</h2>\n<p>If you are a Pocket user, you can connect Feedly to Pocket and replace Read Later with Pocket across the user experience.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/11/Screenshot-2018-11-30-16.16.13.png\" /></figure>\n<h2>New Codebase</h2>\n<p>We have entirely re-implemented the application on a new technology stack.  With a new, modern foundation in place, we are able to iterate faster. For those who are curious, the new app is built using Streets microservices, React for the UI components, and some native extensions when needed.</p>\n<h2>Built collaboratively with 4,000 Feedly users</h2>\n<p>We really enjoyed building the new Feedly in close collaboration with 4,000 Feedly users who volunteered time, expertise, and energy. Your ideas, feedback, and bug reports were critical to the success of the redesign. You’ve helped make Feedly better for everyone.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/Screenshot-2018-12-01-15.00.32.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<p>We are going to double down on this more collaborative and transparent dev process. You can <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/slack-community/\">join the Dev Team and Lab community</a> on Slack and you can <a href=\"https://trello.com/b/bPZDVlwx/feedly-mobileai-lab\">view the roadmap</a> and <a href=\"https://trello.com/b/bPZDVlwx/feedly-mobileai-lab\">upvote features on Trello</a>.</p>\n<p>Finally, if for some reason you prefer the old design, you can look for The more articles you save to a board, the greater the accuracy of Leo&#8217;s like board priorities. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>We are excited to announce a new version of the Feedly Mini Chrome browser extension that makes following sources and saving articles even easier.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Saving an article to one of your Feedly Boards</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>One of the popular feature requests for Feedly Mini pages to one of your Feedly boards</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>In version 5, if you have access to the annotation features, you will be able to add a note to the article you are saving to your boards.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are part of Feedly Teams and have connected Feedly Teams with Slack, you will be able to mention a teammate or a Slack channel directly in Feedly mini and quickly notify your teammates.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Following a new source</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We are also bringing the power of our new discovery experience to Feedly Mini v5.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img source</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Let&#8217;s imagine that you are browsing the Web and you discovered a new source you want to follow in Feedly.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you click on the Feedly Mini icon, Feedly Mini will automatically discover the RSS feed for the page you are reading and show you a popup with information about that source. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can click on Follow in Feedly to preview the RSS in Feedly and add it to one of your feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also click on Explore to tap into the collective wisdom of the Feedly community and determine what are the sources that user often co-read with the source you are looking at.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>No more having to look at the source page to find an RSS URL and manually searching for that URL to be able to add it to one of your feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\"><h2><div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2><p><a We decided as part of the premium fonts project to add support for <a href=\"https://www.opendyslexic.org/\">Open Dyslexic</a> and see if switching to that font can help with the decoding or not. If you are suffering from Dyslexia and want to provide us feedback on how we could help make Feedly better, please join <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/slack-community/\">the Feedly Lab</a>. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Google Noto and support for more languages</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Last but not least, we are have added support for the <a href=\"https://www.google.com/get/noto/\">Google Noto</a>, which is a beautiful font which works well across lots of languages. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"473\" height=\"1024\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/IMG_5512-473x1024.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-11255\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/IMG_5512-473x1024.png 473w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/IMG_5512-139x300.png 139w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/IMG_5512-768x1663.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/IMG_5512.png 1125w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 473px) 100vw, 473px\" /><figcaption>Google Noto</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are consuming lots of international content and need a font preference that works across lots of languages, it might be a very good choice. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Pick what feels the most comfortable</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>On mobile, you can use the Aa menu which is available in the article viewer to change your font settings (and theme). title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p><p>Listening to the murmurs in the Lab Slack channel, it seems that controlling the density of the articles is important to the community. Some users like to see a mix of images with the article summary, some people prefer to see only text, some people want more density, some less. In Experiment 08, we took that feedback into account and added a new density preference which can be applied to text only, magazine, and card views. The result is more control over how you want to consume your feeds.</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/Screenshot-2018-10-15-10.19.34.png\" /></figure>\n<p>Note: The view and density settings can be configured for each source, feed, or board. There is also a global option in the app settings.</p>\n<h2>New icons</h2>\n<p>As part of Experiment 08, we are pushing out the new set of icons (designed by <a href=\"https://dribbble.com/Betraydan\">the talented Daniel Klopper</a>)</p>\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple \"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/image-20.png\" /><figcaption></figcaption></figure>\n<h2>Polish and bug fixes</h2>\n<p>The team also took advantage of the Experiment 08 build to fix the following bugs and rough edges:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Added button to go from no unread to all articles (<a href=\"https://trello.com/c/x4mCRUnc/30-no-unread-all-read\">Thank you Daron, John, Rogerio</a>)</li>\n<li>Return to feed list after swiping the last/first article (<a href=\"https://trello.com/c/6cTO3mpo/179-return-to-feed-list-after-last-article-swipe\">Thank you Peter &#38; You will have to re-select auto-mark as read on scroll in the mobile settings if you want to activate it.</li>\n<li>Improved discover search auto-completion history experience (<a href=\"https://trello.com/c/6QH53lON/146-auto-completion-and-search-history\">Thank you </a>Jesse)</li>\n<li>We polished the back mode of the paged scrolling option (Thank you #paged-scrolling)</li>\n<li>We fixed the conflict between the text selection and the close gestures</li>\n<li>Refreshing the All page after mark as read in the All page footer (<a href=\"https://trello.com/c/bgYGm1Yi/204-refresh-the-all-page-after-tapping-mark-as-read-in-the-footer\">Thank you Dallas</a>)</li>\n<li>Fixed rename source bug (<a href=\"https://trello.com/c/RPJiSsoZ/211-rename-source-bug\">Thank you Dallas</a>)</li>\n<li>Make discover language sticky (Thank you Eduardo)</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Next: Switching the Classic App and the Lab App</h2>\n<p>The next two weeks are about fixing bugs and rough edges and getting to the point where we can replace the classic app with the new lab app. <span style=\"color: #ff0000;\"><strong>Your feedback is going to be extremely useful during that time.</strong> <strong>Once you have 48.0.2 installed, if you experience any bug or run into a part of the experience which does not feel polished, please add a message to the #bugs Slack channel</strong></span>. title=\"Buffer\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p> \n <p>Broad business and tech publications produce hundreds of articles per week. Not all those articles are relevant to the topics, companies, or products you care about. Manually filtering out the noise can be overwhelming and time-consuming. </p> \n <p>Relevance is a problem we are very passionate about. We have spent the last two years designing and building Leo, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo\">your AI research assistant</a> to help declutter your feeds and save time.</p> \n <p>Unlike opaque recommendation engines, Leo has&nbsp;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo\">a set of skills</a> that let you define and control what is relevant to you.</p> \n <p>We are excited to show you how the <strong>Leo Topic skill</strong> lets you track specific topics, companies, and keywords in your feeds.</p> \n <div class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-button webfeeds-actions\">\n  <h2>\n   <div class=\"title\"></div><span class=\"sub\"></span></h2>\n  <p><a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/leo\" class=\"button accent\">GET LEO TOPICS NOW</a></p>\n </div> \n <p>Let’s get started!</p> \n <h2>Companies, people, and products</h2> \n <p>Leo knows about all the companies, people, and products listed in Wikipedia and in the news. You can ask Leo to look for any of those named entities (and their known aliases) and prioritize articles that are a match. </p> \n <p>You can, for example, look for mentions of your competitors or prospects in your industry or tech feeds.</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-8.54.53-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to prioritize mentions of Tesla across a set of trusted business sources\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <h2>Smart Topics</h2> \n <p>Leo understands how to recognize articles about hundreds of “smart” topics (like artificial intelligence, cybersecurity, blockchain, energy, health, etc..). He’ll be looking for thousands of different terms related to that smart topic. We designed smart topics because an article can be about artificial intelligence without including the term “artificial intelligence”.</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-8.52.43-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to prioritize #AI across a set of broad business sources\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>We continuously teach Leo new smart topics. If there is a specific topic you would like to sponsor, please email <a href=\"mailto:leo@feedly.com\">leo@feedly.com</a> </p> \n <h2>Keyword matches</h2> \n <p>You can also ask Leo to look for exact matches of a keyword you are interested in. In this mode, Leo behaves like <a href=\"https://feedly.com/i/leo\">a saved search</a>.</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-9.00.51-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to look for exact matches of the “downsizing” keyword in your business feeds\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <h2>Refine with AND and OR</h2> \n <p>You can design more sophisticated priorities by combining multiple topics using AND and OR. AND means that both of the topics need to be present. OR means that either of the topics needs to be present.</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-9.06.07-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to look for mentions of DNA or CRISPER and cancer in your health industry feeds\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <h2>Combine with other skills</h2> \n <p>The topic skill can be composed with all the other Leo skills allowing you, for example, to easily prioritize articles that reference a product launch (business event skill) while also being related to #artificial intelligence (topic skill)</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-9.11.00-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to prioritize product launch articles related to #AI\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <p>Or high severity software vulnerabilities (cybersecurity skill) related to docker (topic skill)</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Screen-Shot-2019-11-06-at-9.25.44-PM.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Train Leo to prioritize critical Docker vulnerabilities\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <h2>Continuously learning</h2> \n <p>You can use the Leo “less like this” down arrow to correct Leo when a topic detection is incorrect. This feedback is channeled to the Feedly ML Team and to the datasets used to train Leo, making topics increasingly more accurate and relevant over time.</p> \n <figure class=\"wp-block-gts-feedly-image wp-block-image\">\n  <figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\">\n   <img src=\"http://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Tech-2.png\" />\n   <figcaption></figcaption>\n  </figure>\n  <figcaption>\n   Leo continuously learns from your feedback\n  </figcaption>\n </figure> \n <h2><strong>Train Your Leo Now</strong></h2> \n <p>We are excited to see many Feedly users declutter their feeds and dig deeper into the topics and trends that matter to them. incorrect. privacy</span>. <strong>It is an optional feature</strong>: If you are happy with your existing login, you can ignore this post and continue to use your existing login without making any changes.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-7144\"></span></p>\n<p><strong>Adding a feedly Login to your existing login options is easy:</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Go to <a href=\"http://feedly.com/i/logins\" for your feedly login</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Once you have added a feedly Login to your account, you may choose to remove the previously used social logins. ins-del multiReplace\" id=\"11\" data-gr-id=\"11\">duplicat</g>e articles.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This happens, for example, when you have overlapping keyword alerts where two different keywords exist in the same article. It also happens when some sources publish the same articles into different RSS feeds. Finally, it happens a lot when a company issues a press release and other sources publish that press release with some minor changes.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"webfeeds-frame-simple webfeeds-size-large\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"621\" src=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Screenshot-2019-01-29-15.20.33-1024x621.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-11243\" srcset=\"https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Screenshot-2019-01-29-15.20.33-1024x621.png 1024w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Screenshot-2019-01-29-15.20.33-300x182.png 300w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Screenshot-2019-01-29-15.20.33-768x465.png 768w, https://blog.feedly.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Screenshot-2019-01-29-15.20.33-1200x727.png 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Giving you the tools and control to tune your feeds is something we care passionately about. Today, we are excited to announce the beta release of a new <a href=\"https://blog.feedly.com/leo/\">Leo</a> skill called Deduplication.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>What is deduplication? </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>This skill helps Leo detect that multiple articles are near exact duplicates of each other and cut that noise from your feeds. On the Web version of Feedly, you will see a small notification at the bottom right of your screen each time Leo removes duplicate from your feeds.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Which language does deduplication work on?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The Leo deduplication skill works across all languages?</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Which Feedly plan does this skill require?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Because processing duplicates at scale is expensive, this skill will be initially rolled out as part of the Feedly Teams plan.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are part of Feedly Teams, there is a preference knob in&#160;<a href=\"https://feedly.com/b/account/leo\">the Leo settings page</a> to disable this skill.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Beyond near exact duplicates</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The deduplication skill is focusing on near exact duplicates. These are articles which have 85% or more overlap. We are working on a different skill called Business Events for articles which are reporting on the same event but with different content. In the case of business events, the content will be grouped instead of being removed.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Thank you!</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>We want to thank you <a
